"56" 45 "<CHAPTER I. Mrs. Rachel Lynde is Surprised>"
"57" 45 ""
"58" 45 ""
"59" 45 "MRS. Rachel Lynde lived just where the Avonlea main road dipped down"
"60" 45 "into a little hollow, fringed with alders and ladies’ eardrops and"
"61" 45 "traversed by a brook that had its source away back in the woods of the"
"62" 45 "old Cuthbert place; it was reputed to be an intricate, headlong brook"
"63" 45 "in its earlier course through those woods, with dark secrets of pool"
"64" 45 "and cascade; but by the time it reached Lynde’s Hollow it was a quiet,"
"65" 45 "well-conducted little stream, for not even a brook could run past Mrs."
"66" 45 "Rachel Lynde’s door without due regard for decency and decorum; it"
"67" 45 "probably was conscious that Mrs. Rachel was sitting at her window,"
"68" 45 "keeping a sharp eye on everything that passed, from brooks and children"
"69" 45 "up, and that if she noticed anything odd or out of place she would never"
"70" 45 "rest until she had ferreted out the whys and wherefores thereof."
"71" 45 ""
"72" 45 "There are plenty of people in Avonlea and out of it, who can attend"
"73" 45 "closely to their neighbor’s business by dint of neglecting their own;"
"74" 45 "but Mrs. Rachel Lynde was one of those capable creatures who can manage"
"75" 45 "their own concerns and those of other folks into the bargain. She was a"
"76" 45 "notable housewife; her work was always done and well done; she “ran” the"
"77" 45 "Sewing Circle, helped run the Sunday-school, and was the strongest prop"
"78" 45 "of the Church Aid Society and Foreign Missions Auxiliary. Yet with all"
"79" 45 "this Mrs. Rachel found abundant time to sit for hours at her kitchen"
"80" 45 "window, knitting “cotton warp” quilts--she had knitted sixteen of them,"
"81" 45 "as Avonlea housekeepers were wont to tell in awed voices--and keeping"
"82" 45 "a sharp eye on the main road that crossed the hollow and wound up"
"83" 45 "the steep red hill beyond. Since Avonlea occupied a little triangular"
"84" 45 "peninsula jutting out into the Gulf of St. Lawrence with water on two"
"85" 45 "sides of it, anybody who went out of it or into it had to pass over that"
"86" 45 "hill road and so run the unseen gauntlet of Mrs. Rachel’s all-seeing"
"87" 45 "eye."
"88" 45 ""
"89" 45 "She was sitting there one afternoon in early June. The sun was coming in"
"90" 45 "at the window warm and bright; the orchard on the slope below the house"
"91" 45 "was in a bridal flush of pinky-white bloom, hummed over by a myriad of"
"92" 45 "bees. Thomas Lynde--a meek little man whom Avonlea people called “Rachel"
"93" 45 "Lynde’s husband”--was sowing his late turnip seed on the hill field"
"94" 45 "beyond the barn; and Matthew Cuthbert ought to have been sowing his on"
"95" 45 "the big red brook field away over by Green Gables. Mrs. Rachel knew"
"96" 45 "that he ought because she had heard him tell Peter Morrison the evening"
"97" 45 "before in William J. Blair’s store over at Carmody that he meant to sow"
"98" 45 "his turnip seed the next afternoon. Peter had asked him, of course, for"
"99" 45 "Matthew Cuthbert had never been known to volunteer information about"
"100" 45 "anything in his whole life."
"101" 45 ""
"102" 45 "And yet here was Matthew Cuthbert, at half-past three on the afternoon"
"103" 45 "of a busy day, placidly driving over the hollow and up the hill;"
"104" 45 "moreover, he wore a white collar and his best suit of clothes, which was"
"105" 45 "plain proof that he was going out of Avonlea; and he had the buggy"
"106" 45 "and the sorrel mare, which betokened that he was going a considerable"
"107" 45 "distance. Now, where was Matthew Cuthbert going and why was he going"
"108" 45 "there?"
"109" 45 ""
"110" 45 "Had it been any other man in Avonlea, Mrs. Rachel, deftly putting this"
"111" 45 "and that together, might have given a pretty good guess as to both"
"112" 45 "questions. But Matthew so rarely went from home that it must be"
"113" 45 "something pressing and unusual which was taking him; he was the shyest"
"114" 45 "man alive and hated to have to go among strangers or to any place where"
"115" 45 "he might have to talk. Matthew, dressed up with a white collar and"
"116" 45 "driving in a buggy, was something that didn’t happen often. Mrs. Rachel,"
"117" 45 "ponder as she might, could make nothing of it and her afternoon’s"
"118" 45 "enjoyment was spoiled."
"119" 45 ""
"120" 45 "“I’ll just step over to Green Gables after tea and find out from Marilla"
"121" 45 "where he’s gone and why,” the worthy woman finally concluded. “He"
"122" 45 "doesn’t generally go to town this time of year and he _never_ visits; if"
"123" 45 "he’d run out of turnip seed he wouldn’t dress up and take the buggy to"
"124" 45 "go for more; he wasn’t driving fast enough to be going for a doctor."
"125" 45 "Yet something must have happened since last night to start him off. I’m"
"126" 45 "clean puzzled, that’s what, and I won’t know a minute’s peace of mind or"
"127" 45 "conscience until I know what has taken Matthew Cuthbert out of Avonlea"
"128" 45 "today.”"
"129" 45 ""
"130" 45 "Accordingly after tea Mrs. Rachel set out; she had not far to go; the"
"131" 45 "big, rambling, orchard-embowered house where the Cuthberts lived was a"
"132" 45 "scant quarter of a mile up the road from Lynde’s Hollow. To be sure, the"
"133" 45 "long lane made it a good deal further. Matthew Cuthbert’s father, as"
"134" 45 "shy and silent as his son after him, had got as far away as he possibly"
"135" 45 "could from his fellow men without actually retreating into the woods"
"136" 45 "when he founded his homestead. Green Gables was built at the furthest"
"137" 45 "edge of his cleared land and there it was to this day, barely visible"
"138" 45 "from the main road along which all the other Avonlea houses were so"
"139" 45 "sociably situated. Mrs. Rachel Lynde did not call living in such a place"
"140" 45 "_living_ at all."
"141" 45 ""
"142" 45 "“It’s just _staying_, that’s what,” she said as she stepped along the"
"143" 45 "deep-rutted, grassy lane bordered with wild rose bushes. “It’s no wonder"
"144" 45 "Matthew and Marilla are both a little odd, living away back here by"
"145" 45 "themselves. Trees aren’t much company, though dear knows if they were"
"146" 45 "there’d be enough of them. I’d ruther look at people. To be sure, they"
"147" 45 "seem contented enough; but then, I suppose, they’re used to it. A body"
"148" 45 "can get used to anything, even to being hanged, as the Irishman said.”"
"149" 45 ""
"150" 45 "With this Mrs. Rachel stepped out of the lane into the backyard of Green"
"151" 45 "Gables. Very green and neat and precise was that yard, set about on one"
"152" 45 "side with great patriarchal willows and the other with prim Lombardies."
"153" 45 "Not a stray stick nor stone was to be seen, for Mrs. Rachel would have"
"154" 45 "seen it if there had been. Privately she was of the opinion that Marilla"
"155" 45 "Cuthbert swept that yard over as often as she swept her house. One could"
"156" 45 "have eaten a meal off the ground without over-brimming the proverbial"
"157" 45 "peck of dirt."
"158" 45 ""
"159" 45 "Mrs. Rachel rapped smartly at the kitchen door and stepped in"
"160" 45 "when bidden to do so. The kitchen at Green Gables was a cheerful"
"161" 45 "apartment--or would have been cheerful if it had not been so painfully"
"162" 45 "clean as to give it something of the appearance of an unused parlor. Its"
"163" 45 "windows looked east and west; through the west one, looking out on"
"164" 45 "the back yard, came a flood of mellow June sunlight; but the east one,"
"165" 45 "whence you got a glimpse of the bloom white cherry-trees in the left"
"166" 45 "orchard and nodding, slender birches down in the hollow by the brook,"
"167" 45 "was greened over by a tangle of vines. Here sat Marilla Cuthbert, when"
"168" 45 "she sat at all, always slightly distrustful of sunshine, which seemed to"
"169" 45 "her too dancing and irresponsible a thing for a world which was meant to"
"170" 45 "be taken seriously; and here she sat now, knitting, and the table behind"
"171" 45 "her was laid for supper."
"172" 45 ""
"173" 45 "Mrs. Rachel, before she had fairly closed the door, had taken a mental"
"174" 45 "note of everything that was on that table. There were three plates laid,"
"175" 45 "so that Marilla must be expecting some one home with Matthew to tea; but"
"176" 45 "the dishes were everyday dishes and there was only crab-apple preserves"
"177" 45 "and one kind of cake, so that the expected company could not be any"
"178" 45 "particular company. Yet what of Matthew’s white collar and the sorrel"
"179" 45 "mare? Mrs. Rachel was getting fairly dizzy with this unusual mystery"
"180" 45 "about quiet, unmysterious Green Gables."
"181" 45 ""
"182" 45 "“Good evening, Rachel,” Marilla said briskly. “This is a real fine"
"183" 45 "evening, isn’t it? Won’t you sit down? How are all your folks?”"
"184" 45 ""
"185" 45 "Something that for lack of any other name might be called friendship"
"186" 45 "existed and always had existed between Marilla Cuthbert and Mrs. Rachel,"
"187" 45 "in spite of--or perhaps because of--their dissimilarity."
"188" 45 ""
"189" 45 "Marilla was a tall, thin woman, with angles and without curves; her dark"
"190" 45 "hair showed some gray streaks and was always twisted up in a hard little"
"191" 45 "knot behind with two wire hairpins stuck aggressively through it. She"
"192" 45 "looked like a woman of narrow experience and rigid conscience, which she"
"193" 45 "was; but there was a saving something about her mouth which, if it had"
"194" 45 "been ever so slightly developed, might have been considered indicative"
"195" 45 "of a sense of humor."
"196" 45 ""
"197" 45 "“We’re all pretty well,” said Mrs. Rachel. “I was kind of afraid _you_"
"198" 45 "weren’t, though, when I saw Matthew starting off today. I thought maybe"
"199" 45 "he was going to the doctor’s.”"
"200" 45 ""
"201" 45 "Marilla’s lips twitched understandingly. She had expected Mrs."
"202" 45 "Rachel up; she had known that the sight of Matthew jaunting off so"
"203" 45 "unaccountably would be too much for her neighbor’s curiosity."
"204" 45 ""
"205" 45 "“Oh, no, I’m quite well although I had a bad headache yesterday,” she"
"206" 45 "said. “Matthew went to Bright River. We’re getting a little boy from an"
"207" 45 "orphan asylum in Nova Scotia and he’s coming on the train tonight.”"
"208" 45 ""
"209" 45 "If Marilla had said that Matthew had gone to Bright River to meet a"
"210" 45 "kangaroo from Australia Mrs. Rachel could not have been more astonished."
"211" 45 "She was actually stricken dumb for five seconds. It was unsupposable"
"212" 45 "that Marilla was making fun of her, but Mrs. Rachel was almost forced to"
"213" 45 "suppose it."
"214" 45 ""
"215" 45 "“Are you in earnest, Marilla?” she demanded when voice returned to her."
"216" 45 ""
"217" 45 "“Yes, of course,” said Marilla, as if getting boys from orphan asylums"
"218" 45 "in Nova Scotia were part of the usual spring work on any well-regulated"
"219" 45 "Avonlea farm instead of being an unheard of innovation."
"220" 45 ""
"221" 45 "Mrs. Rachel felt that she had received a severe mental jolt. She thought"
"222" 45 "in exclamation points. A boy! Marilla and Matthew Cuthbert of all people"
"223" 45 "adopting a boy! From an orphan asylum! Well, the world was certainly"
"224" 45 "turning upside down! She would be surprised at nothing after this!"
"225" 45 "Nothing!"
"226" 45 ""
"227" 45 "“What on earth put such a notion into your head?” she demanded"
"228" 45 "disapprovingly."
"229" 45 ""
"230" 45 "This had been done without her advice being asked, and must perforce be"
"231" 45 "disapproved."
"232" 45 ""
"233" 45 "“Well, we’ve been thinking about it for some time--all winter in fact,”"
"234" 45 " returned Marilla. “Mrs. Alexander Spencer was up here one day before"
"235" 45 "Christmas and she said she was going to get a little girl from the"
"236" 45 "asylum over in Hopeton in the spring. Her cousin lives there and Mrs."
"237" 45 "Spencer has visited here and knows all about it. So Matthew and I have"
"238" 45 "talked it over off and on ever since. We thought we’d get a boy. Matthew"
"239" 45 "is getting up in years, you know--he’s sixty--and he isn’t so spry as he"
"240" 45 "once was. His heart troubles him a good deal. And you know how desperate"
"241" 45 "hard it’s got to be to get hired help. There’s never anybody to be had"
"242" 45 "but those stupid, half-grown little French boys; and as soon as you do"
"243" 45 "get one broke into your ways and taught something he’s up and off to the"
"244" 45 "lobster canneries or the States. At first Matthew suggested getting a"
"245" 45 "Home boy. But I said ‘no’ flat to that. ‘They may be all right--I’m not"
"246" 45 "saying they’re not--but no London street Arabs for me,’ I said. ‘Give"
"247" 45 "me a native born at least. There’ll be a risk, no matter who we get. But"
"248" 45 "I’ll feel easier in my mind and sleep sounder at nights if we get a born"
"249" 45 "Canadian.’ So in the end we decided to ask Mrs. Spencer to pick us out"
"250" 45 "one when she went over to get her little girl. We heard last week she"
"251" 45 "was going, so we sent her word by Richard Spencer’s folks at Carmody"
"252" 45 "to bring us a smart, likely boy of about ten or eleven. We decided that"
"253" 45 "would be the best age--old enough to be of some use in doing chores"
"254" 45 "right off and young enough to be trained up proper. We mean to give him"
"255" 45 "a good home and schooling. We had a telegram from Mrs. Alexander Spencer"
"256" 45 "today--the mail-man brought it from the station--saying they were coming"
"257" 45 "on the five-thirty train tonight. So Matthew went to Bright River to"
"258" 45 "meet him. Mrs. Spencer will drop him off there. Of course she goes on to"
"259" 45 "White Sands station herself.”"
"260" 45 ""
"261" 45 "Mrs. Rachel prided herself on always speaking her mind; she proceeded to"
"262" 45 "speak it now, having adjusted her mental attitude to this amazing piece"
"263" 45 "of news."
"264" 45 ""
"265" 45 "“Well, Marilla, I’ll just tell you plain that I think you’re doing a"
"266" 45 "mighty foolish thing--a risky thing, that’s what. You don’t know what"
"267" 45 "you’re getting. You’re bringing a strange child into your house and home"
"268" 45 "and you don’t know a single thing about him nor what his disposition is"
"269" 45 "like nor what sort of parents he had nor how he’s likely to turn out."
"270" 45 "Why, it was only last week I read in the paper how a man and his wife up"
"271" 45 "west of the Island took a boy out of an orphan asylum and he set fire to"
"272" 45 "the house at night--set it _on purpose_, Marilla--and nearly burnt them to"
"273" 45 "a crisp in their beds. And I know another case where an adopted boy used"
"274" 45 "to suck the eggs--they couldn’t break him of it. If you had asked my"
"275" 45 "advice in the matter--which you didn’t do, Marilla--I’d have said for"
"276" 45 "mercy’s sake not to think of such a thing, that’s what.”"
"277" 45 ""
"278" 45 "This Job’s comforting seemed neither to offend nor to alarm Marilla. She"
"279" 45 "knitted steadily on."
"280" 45 ""
"281" 45 "“I don’t deny there’s something in what you say, Rachel. I’ve had some"
"282" 45 "qualms myself. But Matthew was terrible set on it. I could see that, so"
"283" 45 "I gave in. It’s so seldom Matthew sets his mind on anything that when he"
"284" 45 "does I always feel it’s my duty to give in. And as for the risk, there’s"
"285" 45 "risks in pretty near everything a body does in this world. There’s risks"
"286" 45 "in people’s having children of their own if it comes to that--they don’t"
"287" 45 "always turn out well. And then Nova Scotia is right close to the Island."
"288" 45 "It isn’t as if we were getting him from England or the States. He can’t"
"289" 45 "be much different from ourselves.”"
"290" 45 ""
"291" 45 "“Well, I hope it will turn out all right,” said Mrs. Rachel in a tone"
"292" 45 "that plainly indicated her painful doubts. “Only don’t say I didn’t"
"293" 45 "warn you if he burns Green Gables down or puts strychnine in the well--I"
"294" 45 "heard of a case over in New Brunswick where an orphan asylum child did"
"295" 45 "that and the whole family died in fearful agonies. Only, it was a girl"
"296" 45 "in that instance.”"
"297" 45 ""
"298" 45 "“Well, we’re not getting a girl,” said Marilla, as if poisoning wells"
"299" 45 "were a purely feminine accomplishment and not to be dreaded in the case"
"300" 45 "of a boy. “I’d never dream of taking a girl to bring up. I wonder at"
"301" 45 "Mrs. Alexander Spencer for doing it. But there, _she_ wouldn’t shrink"
"302" 45 "from adopting a whole orphan asylum if she took it into her head.”"
"303" 45 ""
"304" 45 "Mrs. Rachel would have liked to stay until Matthew came home with his"
"305" 45 "imported orphan. But reflecting that it would be a good two hours at"
"306" 45 "least before his arrival she concluded to go up the road to Robert"
"307" 45 "Bell’s and tell the news. It would certainly make a sensation second"
"308" 45 "to none, and Mrs. Rachel dearly loved to make a sensation. So she took"
"309" 45 "herself away, somewhat to Marilla’s relief, for the latter felt"
"310" 45 "her doubts and fears reviving under the influence of Mrs. Rachel’s"
"311" 45 "pessimism."
"312" 45 ""
"313" 45 "“Well, of all things that ever were or will be!” ejaculated Mrs. Rachel"
"314" 45 "when she was safely out in the lane. “It does really seem as if I must"
"315" 45 "be dreaming. Well, I’m sorry for that poor young one and no mistake."
"316" 45 "Matthew and Marilla don’t know anything about children and they’ll"
"317" 45 "expect him to be wiser and steadier that his own grandfather, if so be’s"
"318" 45 "he ever had a grandfather, which is doubtful. It seems uncanny to think"
"319" 45 "of a child at Green Gables somehow; there’s never been one there, for"
"320" 45 "Matthew and Marilla were grown up when the new house was built--if they"
"321" 45 "ever _were_ children, which is hard to believe when one looks at them."
"322" 45 "I wouldn’t be in that orphan’s shoes for anything. My, but I pity him,"
"323" 45 "that’s what.”"
"324" 45 ""
"325" 45 "So said Mrs. Rachel to the wild rose bushes out of the fulness of her"
"326" 45 "heart; but if she could have seen the child who was waiting patiently"
"327" 45 "at the Bright River station at that very moment her pity would have been"
"328" 45 "still deeper and more profound."
"329" 45 ""
"330" 45 ""
"331" 45 ""
"332" 45 ""
"333" 45 "<CHAPTER II. Matthew Cuthbert is surprised>"
"334" 45 ""
"335" 45 ""
"336" 45 "MATTHEW Cuthbert and the sorrel mare jogged comfortably over the eight"
"337" 45 "miles to Bright River. It was a pretty road, running along between"
"338" 45 "snug farmsteads, with now and again a bit of balsamy fir wood to drive"
"339" 45 "through or a hollow where wild plums hung out their filmy bloom. The air"
"340" 45 "was sweet with the breath of many apple orchards and the meadows sloped"
"341" 45 "away in the distance to horizon mists of pearl and purple; while"
"342" 45 ""
"343" 45 "     “The little birds sang as if it were"
"344" 45 "     The one day of summer in all the year.”"
"345" 45 ""
"346" 45 "Matthew enjoyed the drive after his own fashion, except during the"
"347" 45 "moments when he met women and had to nod to them--for in Prince Edward"
"348" 45 "island you are supposed to nod to all and sundry you meet on the road"
"349" 45 "whether you know them or not."
"350" 45 ""
"351" 45 "Matthew dreaded all women except Marilla and Mrs. Rachel; he had an"
"352" 45 "uncomfortable feeling that the mysterious creatures were secretly"
"353" 45 "laughing at him. He may have been quite right in thinking so, for he"
"354" 45 "was an odd-looking personage, with an ungainly figure and long iron-gray"
"355" 45 "hair that touched his stooping shoulders, and a full, soft brown beard"
"356" 45 "which he had worn ever since he was twenty. In fact, he had looked"
"357" 45 "at twenty very much as he looked at sixty, lacking a little of the"
"358" 45 "grayness."
"359" 45 ""
"360" 45 "When he reached Bright River there was no sign of any train; he thought"
"361" 45 "he was too early, so he tied his horse in the yard of the small Bright"
"362" 45 "River hotel and went over to the station house. The long platform was"
"363" 45 "almost deserted; the only living creature in sight being a girl who was"
"364" 45 "sitting on a pile of shingles at the extreme end. Matthew, barely noting"
"365" 45 "that it _was_ a girl, sidled past her as quickly as possible without"
"366" 45 "looking at her. Had he looked he could hardly have failed to notice the"
"367" 45 "tense rigidity and expectation of her attitude and expression. She was"
"368" 45 "sitting there waiting for something or somebody and, since sitting and"
"369" 45 "waiting was the only thing to do just then, she sat and waited with all"
"370" 45 "her might and main."
"371" 45 ""
"372" 45 "Matthew encountered the stationmaster locking up the ticket office"
"373" 45 "preparatory to going home for supper, and asked him if the five-thirty"
"374" 45 "train would soon be along."
"375" 45 ""
"376" 45 "“The five-thirty train has been in and gone half an hour ago,” answered"
"377" 45 "that brisk official. “But there was a passenger dropped off for you--a"
"378" 45 "little girl. She’s sitting out there on the shingles. I asked her to"
"379" 45 "go into the ladies’ waiting room, but she informed me gravely that she"
"380" 45 "preferred to stay outside. ‘There was more scope for imagination,’ she"
"381" 45 "said. She’s a case, I should say.”"
"382" 45 ""
"383" 45 "“I’m not expecting a girl,” said Matthew blankly. “It’s a boy I’ve come"
"384" 45 "for. He should be here. Mrs. Alexander Spencer was to bring him over"
"385" 45 "from Nova Scotia for me.”"
"386" 45 ""
"387" 45 "The stationmaster whistled."
"388" 45 ""
"389" 45 "“Guess there’s some mistake,” he said. “Mrs. Spencer came off the train"
"390" 45 "with that girl and gave her into my charge. Said you and your sister"
"391" 45 "were adopting her from an orphan asylum and that you would be along for"
"392" 45 "her presently. That’s all I know about it--and I haven’t got any more"
"393" 45 "orphans concealed hereabouts.”"
"394" 45 ""
"395" 45 "“I don’t understand,” said Matthew helplessly, wishing that Marilla was"
"396" 45 "at hand to cope with the situation."
"397" 45 ""
"398" 45 "“Well, you’d better question the girl,” said the station-master"
"399" 45 "carelessly. “I dare say she’ll be able to explain--she’s got a tongue"
"400" 45 "of her own, that’s certain. Maybe they were out of boys of the brand you"
"401" 45 "wanted.”"
"402" 45 ""
"403" 45 "He walked jauntily away, being hungry, and the unfortunate Matthew was"
"404" 45 "left to do that which was harder for him than bearding a lion in its"

"781" 45 ""
"782" 45 "“That’s it, isn’t it?” she said, pointing."
"783" 45 ""
"784" 45 "Matthew slapped the reins on the sorrel’s back delightedly."
"785" 45 ""
"786" 45 "“Well now, you’ve guessed it! But I reckon Mrs. Spencer described it"
"787" 45 "so’s you could tell.”"
"788" 45 ""
"789" 45 "“No, she didn’t--really she didn’t. All she said might just as well have"
"790" 45 "been about most of those other places. I hadn’t any real idea what it"
"791" 45 "looked like. But just as soon as I saw it I felt it was home. Oh, it"
"792" 45 "seems as if I must be in a dream. Do you know, my arm must be black and"
"793" 45 "blue from the elbow up, for I’ve pinched myself so many times today."
"794" 45 "Every little while a horrible sickening feeling would come over me and"
"795" 45 "I’d be so afraid it was all a dream. Then I’d pinch myself to see if it"
"796" 45 "was real--until suddenly I remembered that even supposing it was only"
"797" 45 "a dream I’d better go on dreaming as long as I could; so I stopped"
"798" 45 "pinching. But it _is_ real and we’re nearly home.”"
"799" 45 ""
"800" 45 "With a sigh of rapture she relapsed into silence. Matthew stirred"
"801" 45 "uneasily. He felt glad that it would be Marilla and not he who would"
"802" 45 "have to tell this waif of the world that the home she longed for was"
"803" 45 "not to be hers after all. They drove over Lynde’s Hollow, where it was"
"804" 45 "already quite dark, but not so dark that Mrs. Rachel could not see them"
"805" 45 "from her window vantage, and up the hill and into the long lane of Green"
"806" 45 "Gables. By the time they arrived at the house Matthew was shrinking from"
"807" 45 "the approaching revelation with an energy he did not understand. It was"
"808" 45 "not of Marilla or himself he was thinking or of the trouble this mistake"
"809" 45 "was probably going to make for them, but of the child’s disappointment."
"810" 45 "When he thought of that rapt light being quenched in her eyes he had"
"811" 45 "an uncomfortable feeling that he was going to assist at murdering"
"812" 45 "something--much the same feeling that came over him when he had to kill"
"813" 45 "a lamb or calf or any other innocent little creature."
"814" 45 ""
"815" 45 "The yard was quite dark as they turned into it and the poplar leaves"
"816" 45 "were rustling silkily all round it."
"817" 45 ""
"818" 45 "“Listen to the trees talking in their sleep,” she whispered, as he"
"819" 45 "lifted her to the ground. “What nice dreams they must have!”"
"820" 45 ""

"822" 45 "goods,” she followed him into the house."
"823" 45 ""

"827" 45 "<CHAPTER III. Marilla Cuthbert is Surprised>"
"828" 45 ""
"829" 45 ""
"830" 45 "MARILLA came briskly forward as Matthew opened the door. But when her"
"831" 45 "eyes fell on the odd little figure in the stiff, ugly dress, with the"
"832" 45 "long braids of red hair and the eager, luminous eyes, she stopped short"
"833" 45 "in amazement."
"834" 45 ""
"835" 45 "“Matthew Cuthbert, who’s that?” she ejaculated. “Where is the boy?”"
"836" 45 ""
"837" 45 "“There wasn’t any boy,” said Matthew wretchedly. “There was only _her_.”"
"838" 45 ""
"839" 45 "He nodded at the child, remembering that he had never even asked her"
"840" 45 "name."
"841" 45 ""
"842" 45 "“No boy! But there _must_ have been a boy,” insisted Marilla. “We sent"
"843" 45 "word to Mrs. Spencer to bring a boy.”"
"844" 45 ""
"845" 45 "“Well, she didn’t. She brought _her_. I asked the station-master. And I"
"846" 45 "had to bring her home. She couldn’t be left there, no matter where the"
"847" 45 "mistake had come in.”"
"848" 45 ""
"849" 45 "“Well, this is a pretty piece of business!” ejaculated Marilla."
"850" 45 ""

"858" 45 "known it was all too beautiful to last. I might have known nobody really"

"864" 45 "the stove. Neither of them knew what to say or do. Finally Marilla"
"865" 45 "stepped lamely into the breach."
"866" 45 ""

"868" 45 ""

"871" 45 "an orphan and had come to a place you thought was going to be home and"
"872" 45 "found that they didn’t want you because you weren’t a boy. Oh, this is"
"873" 45 "the most _tragical_ thing that ever happened to me!”"
"874" 45 ""
"875" 45 "Something like a reluctant smile, rather rusty from long disuse,"
"876" 45 "mellowed Marilla’s grim expression."
"877" 45 ""
"878" 45 "“Well, don’t cry any more. We’re not going to turn you out-of-doors"

"880" 45 "What’s your name?”"
"881" 45 ""
"882" 45 "The child hesitated for a moment."
"883" 45 ""
"884" 45 "“Will you please call me Cordelia?” she said eagerly."
"885" 45 ""
"886" 45 "“_Call_ you Cordelia? Is that your name?”"
"887" 45 ""
"888" 45 "“No-o-o, it’s not exactly my name, but I would love to be called"
"889" 45 "Cordelia. It’s such a perfectly elegant name.”"
"890" 45 ""

"898" 45 ""

"977" 45 ""

"1100" 45 "<CHAPTER IV. Morning at Green Gables>"
"1101" 45 ""
"1102" 45 ""
"1103" 45 "IT was broad daylight when Anne awoke and sat up in bed, staring"
"1104" 45 "confusedly at the window through which a flood of cheery sunshine was"
"1105" 45 "pouring and outside of which something white and feathery waved across"
"1106" 45 "glimpses of blue sky."
"1107" 45 ""
"1108" 45 "For a moment she could not remember where she was. First came a"
"1109" 45 "delightful thrill, as something very pleasant; then a horrible"
"1110" 45 "remembrance. This was Green Gables and they didn’t want her because she"
"1111" 45 "wasn’t a boy!"
"1112" 45 ""
"1113" 45 "But it was morning and, yes, it was a cherry-tree in full bloom outside"
"1114" 45 "of her window. With a bound she was out of bed and across the floor."
"1115" 45 "She pushed up the sash--it went up stiffly and creakily, as if it hadn’t"
"1116" 45 "been opened for a long time, which was the case; and it stuck so tight"
"1117" 45 "that nothing was needed to hold it up."
"1118" 45 ""
"1119" 45 "Anne dropped on her knees and gazed out into the June morning, her eyes"
"1120" 45 "glistening with delight. Oh, wasn’t it beautiful? Wasn’t it a lovely"
"1121" 45 "place? Suppose she wasn’t really going to stay here! She would imagine"
"1122" 45 "she was. There was scope for imagination here."
"1123" 45 ""
"1124" 45 "A huge cherry-tree grew outside, so close that its boughs tapped against"
"1125" 45 "the house, and it was so thick-set with blossoms that hardly a leaf"
"1126" 45 "was to be seen. On both sides of the house was a big orchard, one of"
"1127" 45 "apple-trees and one of cherry-trees, also showered over with blossoms;"
"1128" 45 "and their grass was all sprinkled with dandelions. In the garden below"
"1129" 45 "were lilac-trees purple with flowers, and their dizzily sweet fragrance"
"1130" 45 "drifted up to the window on the morning wind."
"1131" 45 ""
"1132" 45 "Below the garden a green field lush with clover sloped down to the"
"1133" 45 "hollow where the brook ran and where scores of white birches grew,"
"1134" 45 "upspringing airily out of an undergrowth suggestive of delightful"
"1135" 45 "possibilities in ferns and mosses and woodsy things generally. Beyond it"
"1136" 45 "was a hill, green and feathery with spruce and fir; there was a gap in"
"1137" 45 "it where the gray gable end of the little house she had seen from the"
"1138" 45 "other side of the Lake of Shining Waters was visible."
"1139" 45 ""
"1140" 45 "Off to the left were the big barns and beyond them, away down over"
"1141" 45 "green, low-sloping fields, was a sparkling blue glimpse of sea."
"1142" 45 ""
"1143" 45 "Anne’s beauty-loving eyes lingered on it all, taking everything greedily"
"1144" 45 "in. She had looked on so many unlovely places in her life, poor child;"
"1145" 45 "but this was as lovely as anything she had ever dreamed."
"1146" 45 ""
"1147" 45 "She knelt there, lost to everything but the loveliness around her, until"
"1148" 45 "she was startled by a hand on her shoulder. Marilla had come in unheard"
"1149" 45 "by the small dreamer."
"1150" 45 ""
"1151" 45 "“It’s time you were dressed,” she said curtly."
"1152" 45 ""
"1153" 45 "Marilla really did not know how to talk to the child, and her"
"1154" 45 "uncomfortable ignorance made her crisp and curt when she did not mean to"
"1155" 45 "be."
"1156" 45 ""
"1157" 45 "Anne stood up and drew a long breath."
"1158" 45 ""
"1159" 45 "“Oh, isn’t it wonderful?” she said, waving her hand comprehensively at"
"1160" 45 "the good world outside."
"1161" 45 ""
"1162" 45 "“It’s a big tree,” said Marilla, “and it blooms great, but the fruit"
"1163" 45 "don’t amount to much never--small and wormy.”"
"1164" 45 ""
"1165" 45 "“Oh, I don’t mean just the tree; of course it’s lovely--yes, it’s"
"1166" 45 "_radiantly_ lovely--it blooms as if it meant it--but I meant everything,"
"1167" 45 "the garden and the orchard and the brook and the woods, the whole big"
"1168" 45 "dear world. Don’t you feel as if you just loved the world on a morning"
"1169" 45 "like this? And I can hear the brook laughing all the way up here."
"1170" 45 "Have you ever noticed what cheerful things brooks are? They’re always"
"1171" 45 "laughing. Even in winter-time I’ve heard them under the ice. I’m so glad"
"1172" 45 "there’s a brook near Green Gables. Perhaps you think it doesn’t make any"
"1173" 45 "difference to me when you’re not going to keep me, but it does. I shall"
"1174" 45 "always like to remember that there is a brook at Green Gables even if"
"1175" 45 "I never see it again. If there wasn’t a brook I’d be _haunted_ by the"
"1176" 45 "uncomfortable feeling that there ought to be one. I’m not in the depths"
"1177" 45 "of despair this morning. I never can be in the morning. Isn’t it a"
"1178" 45 "splendid thing that there are mornings? But I feel very sad. I’ve just"
"1179" 45 "been imagining that it was really me you wanted after all and that I was"
"1180" 45 "to stay here for ever and ever. It was a great comfort while it lasted."
"1181" 45 "But the worst of imagining things is that the time comes when you have"
"1182" 45 "to stop and that hurts.”"
"1183" 45 ""
"1184" 45 "“You’d better get dressed and come down-stairs and never mind your"
"1185" 45 "imaginings,” said Marilla as soon as she could get a word in edgewise."
"1186" 45 "“Breakfast is waiting. Wash your face and comb your hair. Leave the"
"1187" 45 "window up and turn your bedclothes back over the foot of the bed. Be as"
"1188" 45 "smart as you can.”"
"1189" 45 ""
"1190" 45 "Anne could evidently be smart to some purpose for she was down-stairs"
"1191" 45 "in ten minutes’ time, with her clothes neatly on, her hair brushed and"
"1192" 45 "braided, her face washed, and a comfortable consciousness pervading her"
"1193" 45 "soul that she had fulfilled all Marilla’s requirements. As a matter of"
"1194" 45 "fact, however, she had forgotten to turn back the bedclothes."
"1195" 45 ""
"1196" 45 "“I’m pretty hungry this morning,” she announced as she slipped into the"
"1197" 45 "chair Marilla placed for her. “The world doesn’t seem such a howling"

"1199" 45 "But I like rainy mornings real well, too. All sorts of mornings are"

"1201" 45 "through the day, and there’s so much scope for imagination. But I’m"

"1207" 45 ""

"1210" 45 ""

"1348" 45 "<CHAPTER V. Anne’s History>"
"1349" 45 ""
"1350" 45 ""
"1351" 45 "DO you know,” said Anne confidentially, “I’ve made up my mind to enjoy"
"1352" 45 "this drive. It’s been my experience that you can nearly always enjoy"
"1353" 45 "things if you make up your mind firmly that you will. Of course, you"
"1354" 45 "must make it up _firmly_. I am not going to think about going back to"
"1355" 45 "the asylum while we’re having our drive. I’m just going to think about"
"1356" 45 "the drive. Oh, look, there’s one little early wild rose out! Isn’t it"
"1357" 45 "lovely? Don’t you think it must be glad to be a rose? Wouldn’t it be"
"1358" 45 "nice if roses could talk? I’m sure they could tell us such lovely"
"1359" 45 "things. And isn’t pink the most bewitching color in the world? I love"
"1360" 45 "it, but I can’t wear it. Redheaded people can’t wear pink, not even in"
"1361" 45 "imagination. Did you ever know of anybody whose hair was red when she"
"1362" 45 "was young, but got to be another color when she grew up?”"
"1363" 45 ""

"1367" 45 "Anne sighed."
"1368" 45 ""

"1372" 45 ""

"1380" 45 ""

"1402" 45 "My father’s name was Walter Shirley, and he was a teacher in the"

"1445" 45 ""
"1446" 45 "“Mr. and Mrs. Thomas moved away from Bolingbroke to Marysville, and I"

"1461" 45 ""

"1755" 45 "<CHAPTER VII. Anne Says Her Prayers>"
"1756" 45 ""
"1757" 45 ""
"1758" 45 "WHEN Marilla took Anne up to bed that night she said stiffly:"
"1759" 45 ""
"1760" 45 "“Now, Anne, I noticed last night that you threw your clothes all about"
"1761" 45 "the floor when you took them off. That is a very untidy habit, and I"
"1762" 45 "can’t allow it at all. As soon as you take off any article of clothing"
"1763" 45 "fold it neatly and place it on the chair. I haven’t any use at all for"
"1764" 45 "little girls who aren’t neat.”"
"1765" 45 ""
"1766" 45 "“I was so harrowed up in my mind last night that I didn’t think about my"
"1767" 45 "clothes at all,” said Anne. “I’ll fold them nicely tonight. They always"
"1768" 45 "made us do that at the asylum. Half the time, though, I’d forget, I’d be"
"1769" 45 "in such a hurry to get into bed nice and quiet and imagine things.”"
"1770" 45 ""
"1771" 45 "“You’ll have to remember a little better if you stay here,” admonished"
"1772" 45 "Marilla. “There, that looks something like. Say your prayers now and get"
"1773" 45 "into bed.”"
"1774" 45 ""

"1776" 45 ""
"1777" 45 "Marilla looked horrified astonishment."
"1778" 45 ""
"1779" 45 "“Why, Anne, what do you mean? Were you never taught to say your prayers?"
"1780" 45 "God always wants little girls to say their prayers. Don’t you know who"
"1781" 45 "God is, Anne?”"
"1782" 45 ""
"1783" 45 "“‘God is a spirit, infinite, eternal and unchangeable, in His being,"
"1784" 45 "wisdom, power, holiness, justice, goodness, and truth,’” responded Anne"
"1785" 45 "promptly and glibly."
"1786" 45 ""
"1787" 45 "Marilla looked rather relieved."
"1788" 45 ""

"1790" 45 "heathen. Where did you learn that?”"
"1791" 45 ""

"1797" 45 ""

"1801" 45 ""

"1811" 45 ""

"1821" 45 ""

"1829" 45 "What am I to say?”"
"1830" 45 ""

"1897" 45 "<CHAPTER VIII. Anne’s Bringing-up Is Begun>"
"1898" 45 ""
"1899" 45 ""
"1900" 45 "FOR reasons best known to herself, Marilla did not tell Anne that"
"1901" 45 "she was to stay at Green Gables until the next afternoon. During the"
"1902" 45 "forenoon she kept the child busy with various tasks and watched over her"
"1903" 45 "with a keen eye while she did them. By noon she had concluded that Anne"
"1904" 45 "was smart and obedient, willing to work and quick to learn; her most"
"1905" 45 "serious shortcoming seemed to be a tendency to fall into daydreams in"
"1906" 45 "the middle of a task and forget all about it until such time as she was"
"1907" 45 "sharply recalled to earth by a reprimand or a catastrophe."
"1908" 45 ""
"1909" 45 "When Anne had finished washing the dinner dishes she suddenly confronted"
"1910" 45 "Marilla with the air and expression of one desperately determined to"
"1911" 45 "learn the worst. Her thin little body trembled from head to foot; her"
"1912" 45 "face flushed and her eyes dilated until they were almost black; she"
"1913" 45 "clasped her hands tightly and said in an imploring voice:"
"1914" 45 ""
"1915" 45 "“Oh, please, Miss Cuthbert, won’t you tell me if you are going to send"
"1916" 45 "me away or not? I’ve tried to be patient all the morning, but I really"
"1917" 45 "feel that I cannot bear not knowing any longer. It’s a dreadful feeling."
"1918" 45 "Please tell me.”"
"1919" 45 ""
"1920" 45 "“You haven’t scalded the dishcloth in clean hot water as I told you to"
"1921" 45 "do,” said Marilla immovably. “Just go and do it before you ask any more"
"1922" 45 "questions, Anne.”"
"1923" 45 ""
"1924" 45 "Anne went and attended to the dishcloth. Then she returned to Marilla"
"1925" 45 "and fastened imploring eyes of the latter’s face. “Well,” said Marilla,"
"1926" 45 "unable to find any excuse for deferring her explanation longer, “I"
"1927" 45 "suppose I might as well tell you. Matthew and I have decided to keep"
"1928" 45 "you--that is, if you will try to be a good little girl and show yourself"
"1929" 45 "grateful. Why, child, whatever is the matter?”"
"1930" 45 ""
"1931" 45 "“I’m crying,” said Anne in a tone of bewilderment. “I can’t think why."
"1932" 45 "I’m glad as glad can be. Oh, _glad_ doesn’t seem the right word at all. I"
"1933" 45 "was glad about the White Way and the cherry blossoms--but this! Oh, it’s"
"1934" 45 "something more than glad. I’m so happy. I’ll try to be so good. It"
"1935" 45 "will be uphill work, I expect, for Mrs. Thomas often told me I was"
"1936" 45 "desperately wicked. However, I’ll do my very best. But can you tell me"
"1937" 45 "why I’m crying?”"
"1938" 45 ""

"1943" 45 "fortnight till vacation so it isn’t worth while for you to start before"

"1945" 45 ""

"2216" 45 "<CHAPTER IX. Mrs. Rachel Lynde Is Properly Horrified>"
"2217" 45 ""
"2218" 45 ""
"2219" 45 "ANNE had been a fortnight at Green Gables before Mrs. Lynde arrived to"
"2220" 45 "inspect her. Mrs. Rachel, to do her justice, was not to blame for this."
"2221" 45 "A severe and unseasonable attack of grippe had confined that good lady"
"2222" 45 "to her house ever since the occasion of her last visit to Green Gables."
"2223" 45 "Mrs. Rachel was not often sick and had a well-defined contempt for"
"2224" 45 "people who were; but grippe, she asserted, was like no other illness on"
"2225" 45 "earth and could only be interpreted as one of the special visitations"
"2226" 45 "of Providence. As soon as her doctor allowed her to put her foot"
"2227" 45 "out-of-doors she hurried up to Green Gables, bursting with curiosity to"
"2228" 45 "see Matthew and Marilla’s orphan, concerning whom all sorts of stories"
"2229" 45 "and suppositions had gone abroad in Avonlea."
"2230" 45 ""
"2231" 45 "Anne had made good use of every waking moment of that fortnight. Already"
"2232" 45 "she was acquainted with every tree and shrub about the place. She had"
"2233" 45 "discovered that a lane opened out below the apple orchard and ran up"
"2234" 45 "through a belt of woodland; and she had explored it to its furthest end"
"2235" 45 "in all its delicious vagaries of brook and bridge, fir coppice and wild"
"2236" 45 "cherry arch, corners thick with fern, and branching byways of maple and"
"2237" 45 "mountain ash."
"2238" 45 ""
"2239" 45 "She had made friends with the spring down in the hollow--that wonderful"
"2240" 45 "deep, clear icy-cold spring; it was set about with smooth red sandstones"
"2241" 45 "and rimmed in by great palm-like clumps of water fern; and beyond it was"
"2242" 45 "a log bridge over the brook."
"2243" 45 ""
"2244" 45 "That bridge led Anne’s dancing feet up over a wooded hill beyond, where"

"2733" 45 "dew-wet ferns. Far up in the shadows a cheerful light gleamed out"
"2734" 45 "through the trees from the kitchen at Green Gables. Anne suddenly came"
"2735" 45 "close to Marilla and slipped her hand into the older woman’s hard palm."
"2736" 45 ""
"2737" 45 "“It’s lovely to be going home and know it’s home,” she said. “I love"
"2738" 45 "Green Gables already, and I never loved any place before. No place ever"
"2739" 45 "seemed like home. Oh, Marilla, I’m so happy. I could pray right now and"
"2740" 45 "not find it a bit hard.”"
"2741" 45 ""
"2742" 45 "Something warm and pleasant welled up in Marilla’s heart at touch of"
"2743" 45 "that thin little hand in her own--a throb of the maternity she had"
"2744" 45 "missed, perhaps. Its very unaccustomedness and sweetness disturbed"
"2745" 45 "her. She hastened to restore her sensations to their normal calm by"
"2746" 45 "inculcating a moral."
"2747" 45 ""
"2748" 45 "“If you’ll be a good girl you’ll always be happy, Anne. And you should"
"2749" 45 "never find it hard to say your prayers.”"
"2750" 45 ""
"2751" 45 "“Saying one’s prayers isn’t exactly the same thing as praying,” said"
"2752" 45 "Anne meditatively. “But I’m going to imagine that I’m the wind that is"
"2753" 45 "blowing up there in those tree tops. When I get tired of the trees I’ll"
"2754" 45 "imagine I’m gently waving down here in the ferns--and then I’ll fly over"
"2755" 45 "to Mrs. Lynde’s garden and set the flowers dancing--and then I’ll go"
"2756" 45 "with one great swoop over the clover field--and then I’ll blow over the"
"2757" 45 "Lake of Shining Waters and ripple it all up into little sparkling waves."
"2758" 45 "Oh, there’s so much scope for imagination in a wind! So I’ll not talk"
"2759" 45 "any more just now, Marilla.”"
"2760" 45 ""
"2761" 45 "“Thanks be to goodness for that,” breathed Marilla in devout relief."
"2762" 45 ""
"2763" 45 ""

"2766" 45 "<CHAPTER XI. Anne’s Impressions of Sunday-School>"
"2767" 45 ""
"2768" 45 ""
"2769" 45 "WELL, how do you like them?” said Marilla."
"2770" 45 ""
"2771" 45 "Anne was standing in the gable room, looking solemnly at three new"
"2772" 45 "dresses spread out on the bed. One was of snuffy colored gingham which"
"2773" 45 "Marilla had been tempted to buy from a peddler the preceding summer"
"2774" 45 "because it looked so serviceable; one was of black-and-white checkered"
"2775" 45 "sateen which she had picked up at a bargain counter in the winter; and"
"2776" 45 "one was a stiff print of an ugly blue shade which she had purchased that"
"2777" 45 "week at a Carmody store."
"2778" 45 ""
"2779" 45 "She had made them up herself, and they were all made alike--plain skirts"
"2780" 45 "fulled tightly to plain waists, with sleeves as plain as waist and skirt"
"2781" 45 "and tight as sleeves could be."
"2782" 45 ""
"2783" 45 "“I’ll imagine that I like them,” said Anne soberly."
"2784" 45 ""
"2785" 45 "“I don’t want you to imagine it,” said Marilla, offended. “Oh, I can see"
"2786" 45 "you don’t like the dresses! What is the matter with them? Aren’t they"
"2787" 45 "neat and clean and new?”"
"2788" 45 ""
"2789" 45 "“Yes.”"
"2790" 45 ""
"2791" 45 "“Then why don’t you like them?”"
"2792" 45 ""
"2793" 45 "“They’re--they’re not--pretty,” said Anne reluctantly."
"2794" 45 ""
"2795" 45 "“Pretty!” Marilla sniffed. “I didn’t trouble my head about getting"
"2796" 45 "pretty dresses for you. I don’t believe in pampering vanity, Anne, I’ll"
"2797" 45 "tell you that right off. Those dresses are good, sensible, serviceable"
"2798" 45 "dresses, without any frills or furbelows about them, and they’re all"
"2799" 45 "you’ll get this summer. The brown gingham and the blue print will do"
"2800" 45 "you for school when you begin to go. The sateen is for church and Sunday"
"2801" 45 "school. I’ll expect you to keep them neat and clean and not to tear"
"2802" 45 "them. I should think you’d be grateful to get most anything after those"
"2803" 45 "skimpy wincey things you’ve been wearing.”"
"2804" 45 ""
"2805" 45 "“Oh, I _am_ grateful,” protested Anne. “But I’d be ever so much"

"2807" 45 "Puffed sleeves are so fashionable now. It would give me such a thrill,"

"2809" 45 ""
"2810" 45 "“Well, you’ll have to do without your thrill. I hadn’t any material"

"2813" 45 ""

"2816" 45 ""

"2821" 45 ""
"2822" 45 "Anne clasped her hands and looked at the dresses."
"2823" 45 ""

"2830" 45 ""
"2831" 45 "The next morning warnings of a sick headache prevented Marilla from"

"2833" 45 ""

"2854" 45 ""

"2879" 45 ""

"2966" 45 ""
"2967" 45 "IT was not until the next Friday that Marilla heard the story of the"

"2970" 45 ""

"2974" 45 ""

"2976" 45 ""

"2980" 45 ""

"2984" 45 ""

"2987" 45 ""

"3107" 45 ""

"3727" 45 "<CHAPTER XV. A Tempest in the School Teapot>"
"3728" 45 ""
"3729" 45 ""
"3730" 45 "WHAT a splendid day!” said Anne, drawing a long breath. “Isn’t it good"
"3731" 45 "just to be alive on a day like this? I pity the people who aren’t born"
"3732" 45 "yet for missing it. They may have good days, of course, but they can"
"3733" 45 "never have this one. And it’s splendider still to have such a lovely way"
"3734" 45 "to go to school by, isn’t it?”"
"3735" 45 ""
"3736" 45 "“It’s a lot nicer than going round by the road; that is so dusty"
"3737" 45 "and hot,” said Diana practically, peeping into her dinner basket and"
"3738" 45 "mentally calculating if the three juicy, toothsome, raspberry tarts"
"3739" 45 "reposing there were divided among ten girls how many bites each girl"
"3740" 45 "would have."
"3741" 45 ""
"3742" 45 "The little girls of Avonlea school always pooled their lunches, and"
"3743" 45 "to eat three raspberry tarts all alone or even to share them only with"
"3744" 45 "one’s best chum would have forever and ever branded as “awful mean” the"
"3745" 45 "girl who did it. And yet, when the tarts were divided among ten girls"
"3746" 45 "you just got enough to tantalize you."
"3747" 45 ""
"3748" 45 "The way Anne and Diana went to school _was_ a pretty one. Anne thought"
"3749" 45 "those walks to and from school with Diana couldn’t be improved upon"
"3750" 45 "even by imagination. Going around by the main road would have been so"
"3751" 45 "unromantic; but to go by Lover’s Lane and Willowmere and Violet Vale and"
"3752" 45 "the Birch Path was romantic, if ever anything was."
"3753" 45 ""
"3754" 45 "Lover’s Lane opened out below the orchard at Green Gables and stretched"
"3755" 45 "far up into the woods to the end of the Cuthbert farm. It was the way by"
"3756" 45 "which the cows were taken to the back pasture and the wood hauled home"
"3757" 45 "in winter. Anne had named it Lover’s Lane before she had been a month at"
"3758" 45 "Green Gables."
"3759" 45 ""
"3760" 45 "“Not that lovers ever really walk there,” she explained to Marilla,"
"3761" 45 "“but Diana and I are reading a perfectly magnificent book and there’s a"
"3762" 45 "Lover’s Lane in it. So we want to have one, too. And it’s a very pretty"
"3763" 45 "name, don’t you think? So romantic! We can’t imagine the lovers into it,"
"3764" 45 "you know. I like that lane because you can think out loud there without"
"3765" 45 "people calling you crazy.”"
"3766" 45 ""
"3767" 45 "Anne, starting out alone in the morning, went down Lover’s Lane as far"
"3768" 45 "as the brook. Here Diana met her, and the two little girls went on"
"3769" 45 "up the lane under the leafy arch of maples--“maples are such sociable"
"3770" 45 "trees,” said Anne; “they’re always rustling and whispering to"
"3771" 45 "you”--until they came to a rustic bridge. Then they left the lane"
"3772" 45 "and walked through Mr. Barry’s back field and past Willowmere. Beyond"
"3773" 45 "Willowmere came Violet Vale--a little green dimple in the shadow of Mr."
"3774" 45 "Andrew Bell’s big woods. “Of course there are no violets there now,”"
"3775" 45 " Anne told Marilla, “but Diana says there are millions of them in spring."
"3776" 45 "Oh, Marilla, can’t you just imagine you see them? It actually takes away"
"3777" 45 "my breath. I named it Violet Vale. Diana says she never saw the beat"
"3778" 45 "of me for hitting on fancy names for places. It’s nice to be clever at"
"3779" 45 "something, isn’t it? But Diana named the Birch Path. She wanted to, so"
"3780" 45 "I let her; but I’m sure I could have found something more poetical than"
"3781" 45 "plain Birch Path. Anybody can think of a name like that. But the Birch"
"3782" 45 "Path is one of the prettiest places in the world, Marilla.”"
"3783" 45 ""
"3784" 45 "It was. Other people besides Anne thought so when they stumbled on it."
"3785" 45 "It was a little narrow, twisting path, winding down over a long hill"
"3786" 45 "straight through Mr. Bell’s woods, where the light came down sifted"
"3787" 45 "through so many emerald screens that it was as flawless as the heart"
"3788" 45 "of a diamond. It was fringed in all its length with slim young birches,"
"3789" 45 "white stemmed and lissom boughed; ferns and starflowers and wild"
"3790" 45 "lilies-of-the-valley and scarlet tufts of pigeonberries grew thickly"
"3791" 45 "along it; and always there was a delightful spiciness in the air and"
"3792" 45 "music of bird calls and the murmur and laugh of wood winds in the trees"
"3793" 45 "overhead. Now and then you might see a rabbit skipping across the road"
"3794" 45 "if you were quiet--which, with Anne and Diana, happened about once in"
"3795" 45 "a blue moon. Down in the valley the path came out to the main road and"
"3796" 45 "then it was just up the spruce hill to the school."
"3797" 45 ""
"3798" 45 "The Avonlea school was a whitewashed building, low in the eaves and"
"3799" 45 "wide in the windows, furnished inside with comfortable substantial"
"3800" 45 "old-fashioned desks that opened and shut, and were carved all over their"
"3801" 45 "lids with the initials and hieroglyphics of three generations of school"
"3802" 45 "children. The schoolhouse was set back from the road and behind it was"
"3803" 45 "a dusky fir wood and a brook where all the children put their bottles of"
"3804" 45 "milk in the morning to keep cool and sweet until dinner hour."
"3805" 45 ""
"3806" 45 "Marilla had seen Anne start off to school on the first day of September"
"3807" 45 "with many secret misgivings. Anne was such an odd girl. How would she"
"3808" 45 "get on with the other children? And how on earth would she ever manage"
"3809" 45 "to hold her tongue during school hours?"
"3810" 45 ""
"3811" 45 "Things went better than Marilla feared, however. Anne came home that"
"3812" 45 "evening in high spirits."
"3813" 45 ""
"3814" 45 "“I think I’m going to like school here,” she announced. “I don’t think"
"3815" 45 "much of the master, through. He’s all the time curling his mustache"
"3816" 45 "and making eyes at Prissy Andrews. Prissy is grown up, you know. She’s"
"3817" 45 "sixteen and she’s studying for the entrance examination into Queen’s"
"3818" 45 "Academy at Charlottetown next year. Tillie Boulter says the master is"
"3819" 45 "_dead gone_ on her. She’s got a beautiful complexion and curly brown hair"
"3820" 45 "and she does it up so elegantly. She sits in the long seat at the back"

"3822" 45 "says. But Ruby Gillis says she saw him writing something on her slate"

"3826" 45 ""

"3832" 45 "I hope you were a good girl.”"
"3833" 45 ""
"3834" 45 "“Indeed I was,” said Anne comfortably. “It wasn’t so hard as you might"

"3844" 45 "spelling was disgraceful and he held up my slate so that everybody could"
"3845" 45 "see it, all marked over. I felt so mortified, Marilla; he might have"
"3846" 45 "been politer to a stranger, I think. Ruby Gillis gave me an apple and"
"3847" 45 "Sophia Sloane lent me a lovely pink card with ‘May I see you home?’ on"
"3848" 45 "it. I’m to give it back to her tomorrow. And Tillie Boulter let me wear"
"3849" 45 "her bead ring all the afternoon. Can I have some of those pearl beads"

"3852" 45 "heard Prissy Andrews tell Sara Gillis that I had a very pretty nose."

"3855" 45 "a pretty nose? I know you’ll tell me the truth.”"
"3856" 45 ""
"3857" 45 "“Your nose is well enough,” said Marilla shortly. Secretly she thought"
"3858" 45 "Anne’s nose was a remarkable pretty one; but she had no intention of"
"3859" 45 "telling her so."
"3860" 45 ""
"3861" 45 "That was three weeks ago and all had gone smoothly so far. And now, this"
"3862" 45 "crisp September morning, Anne and Diana were tripping blithely down the"

"3864" 45 ""

"3869" 45 ""

"3872" 45 ""

"4285" 45 "<CHAPTER XVI. Diana Is Invited to Tea with Tragic Results>"
"4286" 45 ""
"4287" 45 ""
"4288" 45 "OCTOBER was a beautiful month at Green Gables, when the birches in the"
"4289" 45 "hollow turned as golden as sunshine and the maples behind the orchard"
"4290" 45 "were royal crimson and the wild cherry trees along the lane put on the"
"4291" 45 "loveliest shades of dark red and bronzy green, while the fields sunned"
"4292" 45 "themselves in aftermaths."
"4293" 45 ""
"4294" 45 "Anne reveled in the world of color about her."
"4295" 45 ""
"4296" 45 "“Oh, Marilla,” she exclaimed one Saturday morning, coming dancing in"
"4297" 45 "with her arms full of gorgeous boughs, “I’m so glad I live in a world"
"4298" 45 "where there are Octobers. It would be terrible if we just skipped from"
"4299" 45 "September to November, wouldn’t it? Look at these maple branches. Don’t"
"4300" 45 "they give you a thrill--several thrills? I’m going to decorate my room"
"4301" 45 "with them.”"
"4302" 45 ""
"4303" 45 "“Messy things,” said Marilla, whose aesthetic sense was not noticeably"
"4304" 45 "developed. “You clutter up your room entirely too much with out-of-doors"

"4306" 45 ""

"4632" 45 "stepped out bareheaded into the chill autumn dusk; very determinedly and"
"4633" 45 "steadily she took her way down through the sere clover field over the"
"4634" 45 "log bridge and up through the spruce grove, lighted by a pale little"
"4635" 45 "moon hanging low over the western woods. Mrs. Barry, coming to the door"
"4636" 45 "in answer to a timid knock, found a white-lipped eager-eyed suppliant on"
"4637" 45 "the doorstep."
"4638" 45 ""

"4640" 45 "dislikes, and her anger was of the cold, sullen sort which is always"
"4641" 45 "hardest to overcome. To do her justice, she really believed Anne had"
"4642" 45 "made Diana drunk out of sheer malice prepense, and she was honestly"
"4643" 45 "anxious to preserve her little daughter from the contamination of"
"4644" 45 "further intimacy with such a child."
"4645" 45 ""

"4647" 45 ""

"4649" 45 ""

"4652" 45 "that kind people had adopted and you had just one bosom friend in all"

"4698" 45 "<CHAPTER XVII. A New Interest in Life>"
"4699" 45 ""
"4700" 45 ""
"4701" 45 "THE next afternoon Anne, bending over her patchwork at the kitchen"
"4702" 45 "window, happened to glance out and beheld Diana down by the Dryad’s"
"4703" 45 "Bubble beckoning mysteriously. In a trice Anne was out of the house"
"4704" 45 "and flying down to the hollow, astonishment and hope struggling in"
"4705" 45 "her expressive eyes. But the hope faded when she saw Diana’s dejected"
"4706" 45 "countenance."
"4707" 45 ""

"4709" 45 ""
"4710" 45 "Diana shook her head mournfully."
"4711" 45 ""

"4713" 45 "and cried and I told her it wasn’t your fault, but it wasn’t any use. I"
"4714" 45 "had ever such a time coaxing her to let me come down and say good-bye to"
"4715" 45 "you. She said I was only to stay ten minutes and she’s timing me by the"
"4716" 45 "clock.”"
"4717" 45 ""

"4719" 45 "tearfully. “Oh, Diana, will you promise faithfully never to forget"
"4720" 45 "me, the friend of your youth, no matter what dearer friends may caress"
"4721" 45 "thee?”"
"4722" 45 ""

"4729" 45 ""

"4933" 45 "<CHAPTER XVIII. Anne to the Rescue>"
"4934" 45 ""
"4935" 45 ""
"4936" 45 "ALL things great are wound up with all things little. At first glance"
"4937" 45 "it might not seem that the decision of a certain Canadian Premier to"
"4938" 45 "include Prince Edward Island in a political tour could have much or"
"4939" 45 "anything to do with the fortunes of little Anne Shirley at Green Gables."
"4940" 45 "But it had."
"4941" 45 ""
"4942" 45 "It was a January the Premier came, to address his loyal supporters and"
"4943" 45 "such of his nonsupporters as chose to be present at the monster mass"
"4944" 45 "meeting held in Charlottetown. Most of the Avonlea people were on"
"4945" 45 "Premier’s side of politics; hence on the night of the meeting nearly"
"4946" 45 "all the men and a goodly proportion of the women had gone to town thirty"
"4947" 45 "miles away. Mrs. Rachel Lynde had gone too. Mrs. Rachel Lynde was a"
"4948" 45 "red-hot politician and couldn’t have believed that the political rally"
"4949" 45 "could be carried through without her, although she was on the opposite"
"4950" 45 "side of politics. So she went to town and took her husband--Thomas would"
"4951" 45 "be useful in looking after the horse--and Marilla Cuthbert with her."
"4952" 45 "Marilla had a sneaking interest in politics herself, and as she thought"
"4953" 45 "it might be her only chance to see a real live Premier, she promptly"
"4954" 45 "took it, leaving Anne and Matthew to keep house until her return the"
"4955" 45 "following day."
"4956" 45 ""
"4957" 45 "Hence, while Marilla and Mrs. Rachel were enjoying themselves hugely"
"4958" 45 "at the mass meeting, Anne and Matthew had the cheerful kitchen at Green"
"4959" 45 "Gables all to themselves. A bright fire was glowing in the old-fashioned"
"4960" 45 "Waterloo stove and blue-white frost crystals were shining on the"
"4961" 45 "windowpanes. Matthew nodded over a _Farmers’ Advocate_ on the sofa and"
"4962" 45 "Anne at the table studied her lessons with grim determination, despite"
"4963" 45 "sundry wistful glances at the clock shelf, where lay a new book that"
"4964" 45 "Jane Andrews had lent her that day. Jane had assured her that it was"
"4965" 45 "warranted to produce any number of thrills, or words to that effect, and"
"4966" 45 "Anne’s fingers tingled to reach out for it. But that would mean Gilbert"
"4967" 45 "Blythe’s triumph on the morrow. Anne turned her back on the clock shelf"
"4968" 45 "and tried to imagine it wasn’t there."
"4969" 45 ""
"4970" 45 "“Matthew, did you ever study geometry when you went to school?”"
"4971" 45 ""
"4972" 45 "“Well now, no, I didn’t,” said Matthew, coming out of his doze with a"
"4973" 45 "start."
"4974" 45 ""
"4975" 45 "“I wish you had,” sighed Anne, “because then you’d be able to sympathize"
"4976" 45 "with me. You can’t sympathize properly if you’ve never studied it. It is"
"4977" 45 "casting a cloud over my whole life. I’m such a dunce at it, Matthew.”"
"4978" 45 ""

"4981" 45 "that you was the smartest scholar in school and was making rapid"
"4982" 45 "progress. ‘Rapid progress’ was his very words. There’s them as runs down"
"4983" 45 "Teddy Phillips and says he ain’t much of a teacher, but I guess he’s all"
"4984" 45 "right.”"
"4985" 45 ""
"4986" 45 "Matthew would have thought anyone who praised Anne was “all right.”"
"4987" 45 ""

"4990" 45 "then he draws it on the blackboard and puts different letters from what"

"4996" 45 "and that it’s an awful warning to the electors. She says if women were"

"4999" 45 ""
"5000" 45 "“Conservative,” said Matthew promptly. To vote Conservative was part of"

"5278" 45 "<CHAPTER XIX. A Concert a Catastrophe and a Confession>"
"5279" 45 ""
"5280" 45 ""
"5281" 45 "MARILLA, can I go over to see Diana just for a minute?” asked Anne,"

"5732" 45 "<CHAPTER XX. A Good Imagination Gone Wrong>"

"5735" 45 "SPRING had come once more to Green Gables--the beautiful capricious,"
"5736" 45 "reluctant Canadian spring, lingering along through April and May in a"
"5737" 45 "succession of sweet, fresh, chilly days, with pink sunsets and miracles"
"5738" 45 "of resurrection and growth. The maples in Lover’s Lane were red budded"
"5739" 45 "and little curly ferns pushed up around the Dryad’s Bubble. Away up in"
"5740" 45 "the barrens, behind Mr. Silas Sloane’s place, the Mayflowers blossomed"
"5741" 45 "out, pink and white stars of sweetness under their brown leaves. All the"
"5742" 45 "school girls and boys had one golden afternoon gathering them, coming"
"5743" 45 "home in the clear, echoing twilight with arms and baskets full of"
"5744" 45 "flowery spoil."
"5745" 45 ""
"5746" 45 "“I’m so sorry for people who live in lands where there are no"
"5747" 45 "Mayflowers,” said Anne. “Diana says perhaps they have something better,"
"5748" 45 "but there couldn’t be anything better than Mayflowers, could there,"
"5749" 45 "Marilla? And Diana says if they don’t know what they are like they don’t"
"5750" 45 "miss them. But I think that is the saddest thing of all. I think it"
"5751" 45 "would be _tragic_, Marilla, not to know what Mayflowers are like and _not_"
"5752" 45 "to miss them. Do you know what I think Mayflowers are, Marilla? I think"
"5753" 45 "they must be the souls of the flowers that died last summer and this"
"5754" 45 "is their heaven. But we had a splendid time today, Marilla. We had our"
"5755" 45 "lunch down in a big mossy hollow by an old well--such a _romantic_ spot."
"5756" 45 "Charlie Sloane dared Arty Gillis to jump over it, and Arty did because"
"5757" 45 "he wouldn’t take a dare. Nobody would in school. It is very _fashionable_"
"5758" 45 "to dare. Mr. Phillips gave all the Mayflowers he found to Prissy Andrews"
"5759" 45 "and I heard him to say ‘sweets to the sweet.’ He got that out of a"
"5760" 45 "book, I know; but it shows he has some imagination. I was offered some"
"5761" 45 "Mayflowers too, but I rejected them with scorn. I can’t tell you the"
"5762" 45 "person’s name because I have vowed never to let it cross my lips. We"
"5763" 45 "made wreaths of the Mayflowers and put them on our hats; and when the"
"5764" 45 "time came to go home we marched in procession down the road, two by two,"
"5765" 45 "with our bouquets and wreaths, singing ‘My Home on the Hill.’ Oh, it was"
"5766" 45 "so thrilling, Marilla. All Mr. Silas Sloane’s folks rushed out to see us"
"5767" 45 "and everybody we met on the road stopped and stared after us. We made a"
"5768" 45 "real sensation.”"
"5769" 45 ""
"5770" 45 "“Not much wonder! Such silly doings!” was Marilla’s response."
"5771" 45 ""
"5772" 45 "After the Mayflowers came the violets, and Violet Vale was empurpled"
"5773" 45 "with them. Anne walked through it on her way to school with reverent"
"5774" 45 "steps and worshiping eyes, as if she trod on holy ground."
"5775" 45 ""

"5778" 45 "when I’m up in school it’s all different and I care as much as ever."
"5779" 45 "There’s such a lot of different Annes in me. I sometimes think that is"
"5780" 45 "why I’m such a troublesome person. If I was just the one Anne it would"
"5781" 45 "be ever so much more comfortable, but then it wouldn’t be half so"
"5782" 45 "interesting.”"
"5783" 45 ""
"5784" 45 "One June evening, when the orchards were pink blossomed again, when the"
"5785" 45 "frogs were singing silverly sweet in the marshes about the head of the"
"5786" 45 "Lake of Shining Waters, and the air was full of the savor of clover"

"5791" 45 ""

"5966" 45 "DEAR ME, there is nothing but meetings and partings in this world, as"

"5972" 45 ""

"5975" 45 "Marilla."
"5976" 45 ""

"5980" 45 "Phillips, but just as soon as he got up to make his farewell speech she"

"5982" 45 "I tried to hold out, Marilla. I tried to remember the time Mr. Phillips"
"5983" 45 "made me sit with Gil--with a boy; and the time he spelled my name"

"6340" 45 "<CHAPTER XXII. Anne is Invited Out to Tea>"
"6341" 45 ""
"6342" 45 ""
"6343" 45 "AND what are your eyes popping out of your head about. Now?” asked"
"6344" 45 "Marilla, when Anne had just come in from a run to the post office. “Have"

"6349" 45 ""

"6355" 45 ""

"6360" 45 ""

"6476" 45 "<CHAPTER XXIII. Anne Comes to Grief in an Affair of Honor>"
"6477" 45 ""
"6478" 45 ""
"6479" 45 "ANNE had to live through more than two weeks, as it happened. Almost a"
"6480" 45 "month having elapsed since the liniment cake episode, it was high time"
"6481" 45 "for her to get into fresh trouble of some sort, little mistakes, such as"
"6482" 45 "absentmindedly emptying a pan of skim milk into a basket of yarn balls"
"6483" 45 "in the pantry instead of into the pigs’ bucket, and walking clean over"
"6484" 45 "the edge of the log bridge into the brook while wrapped in imaginative"
"6485" 45 "reverie, not really being worth counting."
"6486" 45 ""
"6487" 45 "A week after the tea at the manse Diana Barry gave a party."
"6488" 45 ""
"6489" 45 "“Small and select,” Anne assured Marilla. “Just the girls in our class.”"
"6490" 45 ""
"6491" 45 "They had a very good time and nothing untoward happened until after tea,"
"6492" 45 "when they found themselves in the Barry garden, a little tired of all"
"6493" 45 "their games and ripe for any enticing form of mischief which might"
"6494" 45 "present itself. This presently took the form of “daring.”"
"6495" 45 ""
"6496" 45 "Daring was the fashionable amusement among the Avonlea small fry just"
"6497" 45 "then. It had begun among the boys, but soon spread to the girls, and all"
"6498" 45 "the silly things that were done in Avonlea that summer because the doers"
"6499" 45 "thereof were “dared” to do them would fill a book by themselves."
"6500" 45 ""
"6501" 45 "First of all Carrie Sloane dared Ruby Gillis to climb to a certain point"
"6502" 45 "in the huge old willow tree before the front door; which Ruby Gillis,"
"6503" 45 "albeit in mortal dread of the fat green caterpillars with which said"
"6504" 45 "tree was infested and with the fear of her mother before her eyes if she"
"6505" 45 "should tear her new muslin dress, nimbly did, to the discomfiture of the"
"6506" 45 "aforesaid Carrie Sloane. Then Josie Pye dared Jane Andrews to hop on her"
"6507" 45 "left leg around the garden without stopping once or putting her right"
"6508" 45 "foot to the ground; which Jane Andrews gamely tried to do, but gave out"
"6509" 45 "at the third corner and had to confess herself defeated."
"6510" 45 ""
"6511" 45 "Josie’s triumph being rather more pronounced than good taste permitted,"
"6512" 45 "Anne Shirley dared her to walk along the top of the board fence which"
"6513" 45 "bounded the garden to the east. Now, to “walk” board fences requires"
"6514" 45 "more skill and steadiness of head and heel than one might suppose who"
"6515" 45 "has never tried it. But Josie Pye, if deficient in some qualities"
"6516" 45 "that make for popularity, had at least a natural and inborn gift, duly"
"6517" 45 "cultivated, for walking board fences. Josie walked the Barry fence with"
"6518" 45 "an airy unconcern which seemed to imply that a little thing like that"
"6519" 45 "wasn’t worth a “dare.” Reluctant admiration greeted her exploit, for"
"6520" 45 "most of the other girls could appreciate it, having suffered many things"
"6521" 45 "themselves in their efforts to walk fences. Josie descended from her"
"6522" 45 "perch, flushed with victory, and darted a defiant glance at Anne."
"6523" 45 ""
"6524" 45 "Anne tossed her red braids."
"6525" 45 ""
"6526" 45 "“I don’t think it’s such a very wonderful thing to walk a little, low,"

"6528" 45 "ridgepole of a roof.”"
"6529" 45 ""
"6530" 45 "“I don’t believe it,” said Josie flatly. “I don’t believe anybody could"

"6532" 45 ""
"6533" 45 "“Couldn’t I?” cried Anne rashly."
"6534" 45 ""

"6537" 45 ""
"6538" 45 "Anne turned pale, but there was clearly only one thing to be done. She"
"6539" 45 "walked toward the house, where a ladder was leaning against the kitchen"
"6540" 45 "roof. All the fifth-class girls said, “Oh!” partly in excitement, partly"
"6541" 45 "in dismay."
"6542" 45 ""

"6545" 45 "anything so dangerous.”"
"6546" 45 ""

"6549" 45 "to have my pearl bead ring.”"
"6550" 45 ""

"6552" 45 "balanced herself uprightly on that precarious footing, and started to"

"6720" 45 "<CHAPTER XXIV. Miss Stacy and Her Pupils Get Up a Concert>"
"6721" 45 ""
"6722" 45 ""
"6723" 45 "IT was October again when Anne was ready to go back to school--a"
"6724" 45 "glorious October, all red and gold, with mellow mornings when the"
"6725" 45 "valleys were filled with delicate mists as if the spirit of autumn had"
"6726" 45 "poured them in for the sun to drain--amethyst, pearl, silver, rose, and"
"6727" 45 "smoke-blue. The dews were so heavy that the fields glistened like cloth"
"6728" 45 "of silver and there were such heaps of rustling leaves in the hollows of"
"6729" 45 "many-stemmed woods to run crisply through. The Birch Path was a canopy"
"6730" 45 "of yellow and the ferns were sear and brown all along it. There was a"
"6731" 45 "tang in the very air that inspired the hearts of small maidens tripping,"
"6732" 45 "unlike snails, swiftly and willingly to school; and it _was_ jolly to"
"6733" 45 "be back again at the little brown desk beside Diana, with Ruby Gillis"
"6734" 45 "nodding across the aisle and Carrie Sloane sending up notes and Julia"
"6735" 45 "Bell passing a “chew” of gum down from the back seat. Anne drew a long"
"6736" 45 "breath of happiness as she sharpened her pencil and arranged her picture"
"6737" 45 "cards in her desk. Life was certainly very interesting."
"6738" 45 ""
"6739" 45 "In the new teacher she found another true and helpful friend. Miss Stacy"
"6740" 45 "was a bright, sympathetic young woman with the happy gift of winning and"
"6741" 45 "holding the affections of her pupils and bringing out the best that was"
"6742" 45 "in them mentally and morally. Anne expanded like a flower under this"
"6743" 45 "wholesome influence and carried home to the admiring Matthew and the"
"6744" 45 "critical Marilla glowing accounts of schoolwork and aims."
"6745" 45 ""
"6746" 45 "“I love Miss Stacy with my whole heart, Marilla. She is so ladylike"

"6749" 45 "this afternoon. I just wish you could have been there to hear me recite"

"6751" 45 "told me coming home that the way I said the line, ‘Now for my father’s"

"6870" 45 "<CHAPTER XXV. Matthew Insists on Puffed Sleeves>"
"6871" 45 ""
"6872" 45 ""
"6873" 45 "MATTHEW was having a bad ten minutes of it. He had come into the"
"6874" 45 "kitchen, in the twilight of a cold, gray December evening, and had sat"
"6875" 45 "down in the woodbox corner to take off his heavy boots, unconscious of"
"6876" 45 "the fact that Anne and a bevy of her schoolmates were having a practice"
"6877" 45 "of “The Fairy Queen” in the sitting room. Presently they came trooping"
"6878" 45 "through the hall and out into the kitchen, laughing and chattering"
"6879" 45 "gaily. They did not see Matthew, who shrank bashfully back into the"
"6880" 45 "shadows beyond the woodbox with a boot in one hand and a bootjack in the"
"6881" 45 "other, and he watched them shyly for the aforesaid ten minutes as they"
"6882" 45 "put on caps and jackets and talked about the dialogue and the concert."
"6883" 45 "Anne stood among them, bright eyed and animated as they; but Matthew"
"6884" 45 "suddenly became conscious that there was something about her different"
"6885" 45 "from her mates. And what worried Matthew was that the difference"
"6886" 45 "impressed him as being something that should not exist. Anne had a"
"6887" 45 "brighter face, and bigger, starrier eyes, and more delicate features"
"6888" 45 "than the other; even shy, unobservant Matthew had learned to take note"
"6889" 45 "of these things; but the difference that disturbed him did not consist"
"6890" 45 "in any of these respects. Then in what did it consist?"
"6891" 45 ""
"6892" 45 "Matthew was haunted by this question long after the girls had gone, arm"
"6893" 45 "in arm, down the long, hard-frozen lane and Anne had betaken herself"
"6894" 45 "to her books. He could not refer it to Marilla, who, he felt, would be"
"6895" 45 "quite sure to sniff scornfully and remark that the only difference she"
"6896" 45 "saw between Anne and the other girls was that they sometimes kept their"
"6897" 45 "tongues quiet while Anne never did. This, Matthew felt, would be no"
"6898" 45 "great help."
"6899" 45 ""
"6900" 45 "He had recourse to his pipe that evening to help him study it out, much"
"6901" 45 "to Marilla’s disgust. After two hours of smoking and hard reflection"
"6902" 45 "Matthew arrived at a solution of his problem. Anne was not dressed like"
"6903" 45 "the other girls!"
"6904" 45 ""
"6905" 45 "The more Matthew thought about the matter the more he was convinced that"
"6906" 45 "Anne never had been dressed like the other girls--never since she had"
"6907" 45 "come to Green Gables. Marilla kept her clothed in plain, dark dresses,"
"6908" 45 "all made after the same unvarying pattern. If Matthew knew there was"
"6909" 45 "such a thing as fashion in dress it was as much as he did; but he was"
"6910" 45 "quite sure that Anne’s sleeves did not look at all like the sleeves the"

"7240" 45 "<CHAPTER XXVI. The Story Club Is Formed>"
"7241" 45 ""
"7242" 45 ""
"7243" 45 "JUNIOR Avonlea found it hard to settle down to humdrum existence"
"7244" 45 "again. To Anne in particular things seemed fearfully flat, stale, and"
"7245" 45 "unprofitable after the goblet of excitement she had been sipping for"
"7246" 45 "weeks. Could she go back to the former quiet pleasures of those faraway"
"7247" 45 "days before the concert? At first, as she told Diana, she did not really"
"7248" 45 "think she could."
"7249" 45 ""
"7250" 45 "“I’m positively certain, Diana, that life can never be quite the"
"7251" 45 "same again as it was in those olden days,” she said mournfully, as if"
"7252" 45 "referring to a period of at least fifty years back. “Perhaps after a"
"7253" 45 "while I’ll get used to it, but I’m afraid concerts spoil people for"
"7254" 45 "everyday life. I suppose that is why Marilla disapproves of them."
"7255" 45 "Marilla is such a sensible woman. It must be a great deal better to be"
"7256" 45 "sensible; but still, I don’t believe I’d really want to be a sensible"
"7257" 45 "person, because they are so unromantic. Mrs. Lynde says there is no"
"7258" 45 "danger of my ever being one, but you can never tell. I feel just now"
"7259" 45 "that I may grow up to be sensible yet. But perhaps that is only because"
"7260" 45 "I’m tired. I simply couldn’t sleep last night for ever so long. I just"
"7261" 45 "lay awake and imagined the concert over and over again. That’s one"
"7262" 45 "splendid thing about such affairs--it’s so lovely to look back to them.”"
"7263" 45 ""
"7264" 45 "Eventually, however, Avonlea school slipped back into its old groove"
"7265" 45 "and took up its old interests. To be sure, the concert left traces. Ruby"
"7266" 45 "Gillis and Emma White, who had quarreled over a point of precedence in"
"7267" 45 "their platform seats, no longer sat at the same desk, and a promising"
"7268" 45 "friendship of three years was broken up. Josie Pye and Julia Bell did"
"7269" 45 "not “speak” for three months, because Josie Pye had told Bessie Wright"
"7270" 45 "that Julia Bell’s bow when she got up to recite made her think of a"
"7271" 45 "chicken jerking its head, and Bessie told Julia. None of the Sloanes"
"7272" 45 "would have any dealings with the Bells, because the Bells had declared"
"7273" 45 "that the Sloanes had too much to do in the program, and the Sloanes had"
"7274" 45 "retorted that the Bells were not capable of doing the little they had to"
"7275" 45 "do properly. Finally, Charlie Sloane fought Moody Spurgeon MacPherson,"
"7276" 45 "because Moody Spurgeon had said that Anne Shirley put on airs about"
"7277" 45 "her recitations, and Moody Spurgeon was “licked”; consequently Moody"
"7278" 45 "Spurgeon’s sister, Ella May, would not “speak” to Anne Shirley all the"
"7279" 45 "rest of the winter. With the exception of these trifling frictions, work"
"7280" 45 "in Miss Stacy’s little kingdom went on with regularity and smoothness."
"7281" 45 ""
"7282" 45 "The winter weeks slipped by. It was an unusually mild winter, with so"
"7283" 45 "little snow that Anne and Diana could go to school nearly every day by"
"7284" 45 "way of the Birch Path. On Anne’s birthday they were tripping lightly"
"7285" 45 "down it, keeping eyes and ears alert amid all their chatter, for Miss"
"7286" 45 "Stacy had told them that they must soon write a composition on “A"
