"7488" 45 "<CHAPTER XXVII. Vanity and Vexation of Spirit>"
"7489" 45 ""
"7490" 45 ""
"7491" 45 "MARILLA, walking home one late April evening from an Aid meeting,"
"7492" 45 "realized that the winter was over and gone with the thrill of delight"
"7493" 45 "that spring never fails to bring to the oldest and saddest as well as to"
"7494" 45 "the youngest and merriest. Marilla was not given to subjective analysis"
"7495" 45 "of her thoughts and feelings. She probably imagined that she was"
"7496" 45 "thinking about the Aids and their missionary box and the new carpet"
"7497" 45 "for the vestry room, but under these reflections was a harmonious"
"7498" 45 "consciousness of red fields smoking into pale-purply mists in the"
"7499" 45 "declining sun, of long, sharp-pointed fir shadows falling over the"
"7500" 45 "meadow beyond the brook, of still, crimson-budded maples around a"
"7501" 45 "mirrorlike wood pool, of a wakening in the world and a stir of hidden"
"7502" 45 "pulses under the gray sod. The spring was abroad in the land and"
"7503" 45 "Marilla’s sober, middle-aged step was lighter and swifter because of its"
"7504" 45 "deep, primal gladness."
"7505" 45 ""
"7506" 45 "Her eyes dwelt affectionately on Green Gables, peering through its"
"7507" 45 "network of trees and reflecting the sunlight back from its windows in"
"7508" 45 "several little coruscations of glory. Marilla, as she picked her steps"
"7509" 45 "along the damp lane, thought that it was really a satisfaction to know"
"7510" 45 "that she was going home to a briskly snapping wood fire and a table"
"7511" 45 "nicely spread for tea, instead of to the cold comfort of old Aid meeting"
"7512" 45 "evenings before Anne had come to Green Gables."
"7513" 45 ""
"7514" 45 "Consequently, when Marilla entered her kitchen and found the fire black"
"7515" 45 "out, with no sign of Anne anywhere, she felt justly disappointed and"
"7516" 45 "irritated. She had told Anne to be sure and have tea ready at five"
"7517" 45 "o’clock, but now she must hurry to take off her second-best dress and"
"7518" 45 "prepare the meal herself against Matthew’s return from plowing."
"7519" 45 ""
"7520" 45 "“I’ll settle Miss Anne when she comes home,” said Marilla grimly, as"
"7521" 45 "she shaved up kindlings with a carving knife and with more vim than was"
"7522" 45 "strictly necessary. Matthew had come in and was waiting patiently for"
"7523" 45 "his tea in his corner. “She’s gadding off somewhere with Diana, writing"
"7524" 45 "stories or practicing dialogues or some such tomfoolery, and never"
"7525" 45 "thinking once about the time or her duties. She’s just got to be pulled"
"7526" 45 "up short and sudden on this sort of thing. I don’t care if Mrs. Allan"
"7527" 45 "does say she’s the brightest and sweetest child she ever knew. She may"
"7528" 45 "be bright and sweet enough, but her head is full of nonsense and there’s"
"7529" 45 "never any knowing what shape it’ll break out in next. Just as soon as"
"7530" 45 "she grows out of one freak she takes up with another. But there! Here I"
"7531" 45 "am saying the very thing I was so riled with Rachel Lynde for saying at"
"7532" 45 "the Aid today. I was real glad when Mrs. Allan spoke up for Anne, for"
"7533" 45 "if she hadn’t I know I’d have said something too sharp to Rachel before"
"7534" 45 "everybody. Anne’s got plenty of faults, goodness knows, and far be it"
"7535" 45 "from me to deny it. But I’m bringing her up and not Rachel Lynde, who’d"
"7536" 45 "pick faults in the Angel Gabriel himself if he lived in Avonlea. Just"
"7537" 45 "the same, Anne has no business to leave the house like this when I told"
"7538" 45 "her she was to stay home this afternoon and look after things. I must"
"7539" 45 "say, with all her faults, I never found her disobedient or untrustworthy"
"7540" 45 "before and I’m real sorry to find her so now.”"
"7541" 45 ""
"7542" 45 "“Well now, I dunno,” said Matthew, who, being patient and wise and,"
"7543" 45 "above all, hungry, had deemed it best to let Marilla talk her wrath"
"7544" 45 "out unhindered, having learned by experience that she got through"
"7545" 45 "with whatever work was on hand much quicker if not delayed by untimely"
"7546" 45 "argument. “Perhaps you’re judging her too hasty, Marilla. Don’t call her"
"7547" 45 "untrustworthy until you’re sure she has disobeyed you. Mebbe it can all"

"7549" 45 ""

"7552" 45 "you’d take her part, Matthew. But I’m bringing her up, not you.”"
"7553" 45 ""
"7554" 45 "It was dark when supper was ready, and still no sign of Anne, coming"

"7561" 45 ""

"7570" 45 ""

"7582" 45 ""
"7583" 45 "Anne had slid to the floor in despairing obedience."
"7584" 45 ""

"7586" 45 ""

"7607" 45 ""

"7609" 45 ""

"7612" 45 ""

"7617" 45 ""

"7621" 45 ""
"7622" 45 "“But I didn’t mean to dye it green, Marilla,” protested Anne dejectedly."

"7631" 45 "“Who said? Who are you talking about?”"

"7635" 45 "“Anne Shirley, how often have I told you never to let one of those"

"7638" 45 ""

"7651" 45 "had a very kind heart, for he said that, seeing it was me, he’d sell it"
"7652" 45 "for fifty cents and that was just giving it away. So I bought it, and as"
"7653" 45 "soon as he had gone I came up here and applied it with an old hairbrush"
"7654" 45 "as the directions said. I used up the whole bottle, and oh, Marilla,"
"7655" 45 "when I saw the dreadful color it turned my hair I repented of being"
"7656" 45 "wicked, I can tell you. And I’ve been repenting ever since.”"
"7657" 45 ""
"7658" 45 "“Well, I hope you’ll repent to good purpose,” said Marilla severely,"
"7659" 45 "“and that you’ve got your eyes opened to where your vanity has led you,"
"7660" 45 "Anne. Goodness knows what’s to be done. I suppose the first thing is to"
"7661" 45 "give your hair a good washing and see if that will do any good.”"
"7662" 45 ""
"7663" 45 "Accordingly, Anne washed her hair, scrubbing it vigorously with soap and"
"7664" 45 "water, but for all the difference it made she might as well have been"
"7665" 45 "scouring its original red. The peddler had certainly spoken the truth"
"7666" 45 "when he declared that the dye wouldn’t wash off, however his veracity"
"7667" 45 "might be impeached in other respects."
"7668" 45 ""
"7669" 45 "“Oh, Marilla, what shall I do?” questioned Anne in tears. “I can never"
"7670" 45 "live this down. People have pretty well forgotten my other mistakes--the"
"7671" 45 "liniment cake and setting Diana drunk and flying into a temper with"
"7672" 45 "Mrs. Lynde. But they’ll never forget this. They will think I am not"
"7673" 45 "respectable. Oh, Marilla, ‘what a tangled web we weave when first we"
"7674" 45 "practice to deceive.’ That is poetry, but it is true. And oh, how Josie"
"7675" 45 "Pye will laugh! Marilla, I _cannot_ face Josie Pye. I am the unhappiest"
"7676" 45 "girl in Prince Edward Island.”"
"7677" 45 ""
"7678" 45 "Anne’s unhappiness continued for a week. During that time she went"
"7679" 45 "nowhere and shampooed her hair every day. Diana alone of outsiders knew"
"7680" 45 "the fatal secret, but she promised solemnly never to tell, and it may"
"7681" 45 "be stated here and now that she kept her word. At the end of the week"
"7682" 45 "Marilla said decidedly:"
"7683" 45 ""
"7684" 45 "“It’s no use, Anne. That is fast dye if ever there was any. Your hair"
"7685" 45 "must be cut off; there is no other way. You can’t go out with it looking"
"7686" 45 "like that.”"
"7687" 45 ""
"7688" 45 "Anne’s lips quivered, but she realized the bitter truth of Marilla’s"
"7689" 45 "remarks. With a dismal sigh she went for the scissors."
"7690" 45 ""
"7691" 45 "“Please cut it off at once, Marilla, and have it over. Oh, I feel that"
"7692" 45 "my heart is broken. This is such an unromantic affliction. The girls in"
"7693" 45 "books lose their hair in fevers or sell it to get money for some good"

"7695" 45 "half so much. But there is nothing comforting in having your hair cut"
"7696" 45 "off because you’ve dyed it a dreadful color, is there? I’m going to weep"
"7697" 45 "all the time you’re cutting it off, if it won’t interfere. It seems such"
"7698" 45 "a tragic thing.”"
"7699" 45 ""
"7700" 45 "Anne wept then, but later on, when she went upstairs and looked in the"
"7701" 45 "glass, she was calm with despair. Marilla had done her work thoroughly"
"7702" 45 "and it had been necessary to shingle the hair as closely as possible."
"7703" 45 "The result was not becoming, to state the case as mildly as may be. Anne"
"7704" 45 "promptly turned her glass to the wall."
"7705" 45 ""
"7706" 45 "“I’ll never, never look at myself again until my hair grows,” she"
"7707" 45 "exclaimed passionately."
"7708" 45 ""
"7709" 45 "Then she suddenly righted the glass."
"7710" 45 ""
"7711" 45 "“Yes, I will, too. I’d do penance for being wicked that way. I’ll look"
"7712" 45 "at myself every time I come to my room and see how ugly I am. And I"
"7713" 45 "won’t try to imagine it away, either. I never thought I was vain about"
"7714" 45 "my hair, of all things, but now I know I was, in spite of its being"
"7715" 45 "red, because it was so long and thick and curly. I expect something will"
"7716" 45 "happen to my nose next.”"
"7717" 45 ""
"7718" 45 "Anne’s clipped head made a sensation in school on the following Monday,"
"7719" 45 "but to her relief nobody guessed the real reason for it, not even Josie"

"7722" 45 ""

"7738" 45 ""

"7740" 45 "These headaches of mine are getting worse and worse. I’ll have to see"

"7743" 45 ""
"7744" 45 "Which was Marilla’s way of saying that she liked to hear it."

"7749" 45 "<CHAPTER XXVIII. An Unfortunate Lily Maid>"
"7750" 45 ""
"7751" 45 ""
"7752" 45 "OF course you must be Elaine, Anne,” said Diana. “I could never have"
"7753" 45 "the courage to float down there.”"
"7754" 45 ""
"7755" 45 "“Nor I,” said Ruby Gillis, with a shiver. “I don’t mind floating down"
"7756" 45 "when there’s two or three of us in the flat and we can sit up. It’s fun"
"7757" 45 "then. But to lie down and pretend I was dead--I just couldn’t. I’d die"
"7758" 45 "really of fright.”"
"7759" 45 ""
"7760" 45 "“Of course it would be romantic,” conceded Jane Andrews, “but I know I"
"7761" 45 "couldn’t keep still. I’d be popping up every minute or so to see where I"
"7762" 45 "was and if I wasn’t drifting too far out. And you know, Anne, that would"
"7763" 45 "spoil the effect.”"
"7764" 45 ""
"7765" 45 "“But it’s so ridiculous to have a redheaded Elaine,” mourned Anne. “I’m"
"7766" 45 "not afraid to float down and I’d love to be Elaine. But it’s ridiculous"
"7767" 45 "just the same. Ruby ought to be Elaine because she is so fair and has"
"7768" 45 "such lovely long golden hair--Elaine had ‘all her bright hair streaming"
"7769" 45 "down,’ you know. And Elaine was the lily maid. Now, a red-haired person"
"7770" 45 "cannot be a lily maid.”"
"7771" 45 ""
"7772" 45 "“Your complexion is just as fair as Ruby’s,” said Diana earnestly, “and"
"7773" 45 "your hair is ever so much darker than it used to be before you cut it.”"
"7774" 45 ""
"7775" 45 "“Oh, do you really think so?” exclaimed Anne, flushing sensitively with"
"7776" 45 "delight. “I’ve sometimes thought it was myself--but I never dared to ask"
"7777" 45 "anyone for fear she would tell me it wasn’t. Do you think it could be"
"7778" 45 "called auburn now, Diana?”"
"7779" 45 ""
"7780" 45 "“Yes, and I think it is real pretty,” said Diana, looking admiringly at"
"7781" 45 "the short, silky curls that clustered over Anne’s head and were held in"
"7782" 45 "place by a very jaunty black velvet ribbon and bow."
"7783" 45 ""
"7784" 45 "They were standing on the bank of the pond, below Orchard Slope, where"
"7785" 45 "a little headland fringed with birches ran out from the bank; at its tip"
"7786" 45 "was a small wooden platform built out into the water for the convenience"
"7787" 45 "of fishermen and duck hunters. Ruby and Jane were spending the midsummer"
"7788" 45 "afternoon with Diana, and Anne had come over to play with them."
"7789" 45 ""
"7790" 45 "Anne and Diana had spent most of their playtime that summer on and about"
"7791" 45 "the pond. Idlewild was a thing of the past, Mr. Bell having ruthlessly"
"7792" 45 "cut down the little circle of trees in his back pasture in the spring."
"7793" 45 "Anne had sat among the stumps and wept, not without an eye to the"
"7794" 45 "romance of it; but she was speedily consoled, for, after all, as she and"
"7795" 45 "Diana said, big girls of thirteen, going on fourteen, were too old for"
"7796" 45 "such childish amusements as playhouses, and there were more fascinating"
"7797" 45 "sports to be found about the pond. It was splendid to fish for trout"
"7798" 45 "over the bridge and the two girls learned to row themselves about in the"
"7799" 45 "little flat-bottomed dory Mr. Barry kept for duck shooting."
"7800" 45 ""
"7801" 45 "It was Anne’s idea that they dramatize Elaine. They had studied"
"7802" 45 "Tennyson’s poem in school the preceding winter, the Superintendent of"
"7803" 45 "Education having prescribed it in the English course for the Prince"
"7804" 45 "Edward Island schools. They had analyzed and parsed it and torn it to"
"7805" 45 "pieces in general until it was a wonder there was any meaning at all"
"7806" 45 "left in it for them, but at least the fair lily maid and Lancelot and"
"7807" 45 "Guinevere and King Arthur had become very real people to them, and Anne"
"7808" 45 "was devoured by secret regret that she had not been born in Camelot."
"7809" 45 "Those days, she said, were so much more romantic than the present."
"7810" 45 ""
"7811" 45 "Anne’s plan was hailed with enthusiasm. The girls had discovered that if"
"7812" 45 "the flat were pushed off from the landing place it would drift down"
"7813" 45 "with the current under the bridge and finally strand itself on another"
"7814" 45 "headland lower down which ran out at a curve in the pond. They had often"
"7815" 45 "gone down like this and nothing could be more convenient for playing"
"7816" 45 "Elaine."
"7817" 45 ""
"7818" 45 "“Well, I’ll be Elaine,” said Anne, yielding reluctantly, for, although"
"7819" 45 "she would have been delighted to play the principal character, yet"
"7820" 45 "her artistic sense demanded fitness for it and this, she felt, her"
"7821" 45 "limitations made impossible. “Ruby, you must be King Arthur and Jane"
"7822" 45 "will be Guinevere and Diana must be Lancelot. But first you must be the"
"7823" 45 "brothers and the father. We can’t have the old dumb servitor because"
"7824" 45 "there isn’t room for two in the flat when one is lying down. We must"
"7825" 45 "pall the barge all its length in blackest samite. That old black shawl"
"7826" 45 "of your mother’s will be just the thing, Diana.”"
"7827" 45 ""
"7828" 45 "The black shawl having been procured, Anne spread it over the flat and"
"7829" 45 "then lay down on the bottom, with closed eyes and hands folded over her"
"7830" 45 "breast."
"7831" 45 ""
"7832" 45 "“Oh, she does look really dead,” whispered Ruby Gillis nervously,"
"7833" 45 "watching the still, white little face under the flickering shadows of"

"7836" 45 "abominably wicked.”"
"7837" 45 ""
"7838" 45 "“Ruby, you shouldn’t talk about Mrs. Lynde,” said Anne severely. “It"
"7839" 45 "spoils the effect because this is hundreds of years before Mrs. Lynde"
"7840" 45 "was born. Jane, you arrange this. It’s silly for Elaine to be talking"
"7841" 45 "when she’s dead.”"
"7842" 45 ""
"7843" 45 "Jane rose to the occasion. Cloth of gold for coverlet there was none,"
"7844" 45 "but an old piano scarf of yellow Japanese crepe was an excellent"
"7845" 45 "substitute. A white lily was not obtainable just then, but the effect of"
"7846" 45 "a tall blue iris placed in one of Anne’s folded hands was all that could"
"7847" 45 "be desired."
"7848" 45 ""
"7849" 45 "“Now, she’s all ready,” said Jane. “We must kiss her quiet brows"

"7854" 45 ""
"7855" 45 "The flat was accordingly pushed off, scraping roughly over an old"
"7856" 45 "embedded stake in the process. Diana and Jane and Ruby only waited long"

"7861" 45 ""
"7862" 45 "For a few minutes Anne, drifting slowly down, enjoyed the romance of her"

"7868" 45 "the landing had torn off the strip of batting nailed on the flat. Anne"

"7870" 45 "in a dangerous plight. At this rate the flat would fill and sink long"
"7871" 45 "before it could drift to the lower headland. Where were the oars? Left"
"7872" 45 "behind at the landing!"
"7873" 45 ""
"7874" 45 "Anne gave one gasping little scream which nobody ever heard; she was"
"7875" 45 "white to the lips, but she did not lose her self-possession. There was"
"7876" 45 "one chance--just one."
"7877" 45 ""
"7878" 45 "“I was horribly frightened,” she told Mrs. Allan the next day, “and it"
"7879" 45 "seemed like years while the flat was drifting down to the bridge and the"

"7881" 45 "but I didn’t shut my eyes to pray, for I knew the only way God could"

"7893" 45 "but I didn’t think about that at the time. You don’t think much about"

"7895" 45 "grateful prayer at once and then I gave all my attention to holding on"
"7896" 45 "tight, for I knew I should probably have to depend on human aid to get"
"7897" 45 "back to dry land.”"
"7898" 45 ""
"7899" 45 "The flat drifted under the bridge and then promptly sank in midstream."
"7900" 45 "Ruby, Jane, and Diana, already awaiting it on the lower headland, saw it"
"7901" 45 "disappear before their very eyes and had not a doubt but that Anne"

"7906" 45 "Anne, clinging desperately to her precarious foothold, saw their flying"
"7907" 45 "forms and heard their shrieks. Help would soon come, but meanwhile her"
"7908" 45 "position was a very uncomfortable one."
"7909" 45 ""
"7910" 45 "The minutes passed by, each seeming an hour to the unfortunate lily"
"7911" 45 "maid. Why didn’t somebody come? Where had the girls gone? Suppose they"
"7912" 45 "had fainted, one and all! Suppose nobody ever came! Suppose she grew so"

"7914" 45 "wicked green depths below her, wavering with long, oily shadows, and"

"7916" 45 "possibilities to her."
"7917" 45 ""

"7921" 45 ""

"8028" 45 "cooking. Dyeing my hair cured me of vanity. I never think about my hair"
"8029" 45 "and nose now--at least, very seldom. And today’s mistake is going to"
"8030" 45 "cure me of being too romantic. I have come to the conclusion that it is"
"8031" 45 "no use trying to be romantic in Avonlea. It was probably easy enough in"
"8032" 45 "towered Camelot hundreds of years ago, but romance is not appreciated"
"8033" 45 "now. I feel quite sure that you will soon see a great improvement in me"
"8034" 45 "in this respect, Marilla.”"
"8035" 45 ""
"8036" 45 "“I’m sure I hope so,” said Marilla skeptically."
"8037" 45 ""
"8038" 45 "But Matthew, who had been sitting mutely in his corner, laid a hand on"
"8039" 45 "Anne’s shoulder when Marilla had gone out."
"8040" 45 ""
"8041" 45 "“Don’t give up all your romance, Anne,” he whispered shyly, “a little"
"8042" 45 "of it is a good thing--not too much, of course--but keep a little of it,"
"8043" 45 "Anne, keep a little of it.”"
"8044" 45 ""
"8045" 45 ""
"8046" 45 ""
"8047" 45 ""
"8048" 45 "<CHAPTER XXIX. An Epoch in Anne’s Life>"
"8049" 45 ""
"8050" 45 ""
"8051" 45 "ANNE was bringing the cows home from the back pasture by way of Lover’s"
"8052" 45 "Lane. It was a September evening and all the gaps and clearings in the"
"8053" 45 "woods were brimmed up with ruby sunset light. Here and there the lane"
"8054" 45 "was splashed with it, but for the most part it was already quite shadowy"
"8055" 45 "beneath the maples, and the spaces under the firs were filled with a"
"8056" 45 "clear violet dusk like airy wine. The winds were out in their tops, and"
"8057" 45 "there is no sweeter music on earth than that which the wind makes in the"
"8058" 45 "fir trees at evening."
"8059" 45 ""
"8060" 45 "The cows swung placidly down the lane, and Anne followed them dreamily,"
"8061" 45 "repeating aloud the battle canto from _Marmion_--which had also been part"
"8062" 45 "of their English course the preceding winter and which Miss Stacy had"
"8063" 45 "made them learn off by heart--and exulting in its rushing lines and the"
"8064" 45 "clash of spears in its imagery. When she came to the lines"
"8065" 45 ""
"8066" 45 "       The stubborn spearsmen still made good"
"8067" 45 "       Their dark impenetrable wood,"
"8068" 45 ""
"8069" 45 "she stopped in ecstasy to shut her eyes that she might the better fancy"
"8070" 45 "herself one of that heroic ring. When she opened them again it was to"
"8071" 45 "behold Diana coming through the gate that led into the Barry field and"
"8072" 45 "looking so important that Anne instantly divined there was news to be"
"8073" 45 "told. But betray too eager curiosity she would not."
"8074" 45 ""
"8075" 45 "“Isn’t this evening just like a purple dream, Diana? It makes me so glad"
"8076" 45 "to be alive. In the mornings I always think the mornings are best; but"
"8077" 45 "when evening comes I think it’s lovelier still.”"
"8078" 45 ""
"8079" 45 "“It’s a very fine evening,” said Diana, “but oh, I have such news, Anne."
"8080" 45 "Guess. You can have three guesses.”"
"8081" 45 ""
"8082" 45 "“Charlotte Gillis is going to be married in the church after all and"
"8083" 45 "Mrs. Allan wants us to decorate it,” cried Anne."
"8084" 45 ""
"8085" 45 "“No. Charlotte’s beau won’t agree to that, because nobody ever has been"
"8086" 45 "married in the church yet, and he thinks it would seem too much like a"
"8087" 45 "funeral. It’s too mean, because it would be such fun. Guess again.”"
"8088" 45 ""
"8089" 45 "“Jane’s mother is going to let her have a birthday party?”"
"8090" 45 ""
"8091" 45 "Diana shook her head, her black eyes dancing with merriment."
"8092" 45 ""
"8093" 45 "“I can’t think what it can be,” said Anne in despair, “unless it’s that"
"8094" 45 "Moody Spurgeon MacPherson saw you home from prayer meeting last night."
"8095" 45 "Did he?”"
"8096" 45 ""
"8097" 45 "“I should think not,” exclaimed Diana indignantly. “I wouldn’t be likely"
"8098" 45 "to boast of it if he did, the horrid creature! I knew you couldn’t guess"
"8099" 45 "it. Mother had a letter from Aunt Josephine today, and Aunt Josephine"
"8100" 45 "wants you and me to go to town next Tuesday and stop with her for the"
"8101" 45 "Exhibition. There!”"
"8102" 45 ""
"8103" 45 "“Oh, Diana,” whispered Anne, finding it necessary to lean up against a"
"8104" 45 "maple tree for support, “do you really mean it? But I’m afraid Marilla"
"8105" 45 "won’t let me go. She will say that she can’t encourage gadding about."
"8106" 45 "That was what she said last week when Jane invited me to go with them"
"8107" 45 "in their double-seated buggy to the American concert at the White Sands"
"8108" 45 "Hotel. I wanted to go, but Marilla said I’d be better at home learning"
"8109" 45 "my lessons and so would Jane. I was bitterly disappointed, Diana. I felt"
"8110" 45 "so heartbroken that I wouldn’t say my prayers when I went to bed. But I"
"8111" 45 "repented of that and got up in the middle of the night and said them.”"
"8112" 45 ""
"8113" 45 "“I’ll tell you,” said Diana, “we’ll get Mother to ask Marilla. She’ll be"
"8114" 45 "more likely to let you go then; and if she does we’ll have the time"
"8115" 45 "of our lives, Anne. I’ve never been to an Exhibition, and it’s so"
"8116" 45 "aggravating to hear the other girls talking about their trips. Jane and"
"8117" 45 "Ruby have been twice, and they’re going this year again.”"
"8118" 45 ""
"8119" 45 "“I’m not going to think about it at all until I know whether I can go"
"8120" 45 "or not,” said Anne resolutely. “If I did and then was disappointed, it"
"8121" 45 "would be more than I could bear. But in case I do go I’m very glad my"
"8122" 45 "new coat will be ready by that time. Marilla didn’t think I needed a new"
"8123" 45 "coat. She said my old one would do very well for another winter and"
"8124" 45 "that I ought to be satisfied with having a new dress. The dress is very"
"8125" 45 "pretty, Diana--navy blue and made so fashionably. Marilla always makes"
"8126" 45 "my dresses fashionably now, because she says she doesn’t intend to have"
"8127" 45 "Matthew going to Mrs. Lynde to make them. I’m so glad. It is ever so"
"8128" 45 "much easier to be good if your clothes are fashionable. At least, it is"
"8129" 45 "easier for me. I suppose it doesn’t make such a difference to naturally"
"8130" 45 "good people. But Matthew said I must have a new coat, so Marilla"
"8131" 45 "bought a lovely piece of blue broadcloth, and it’s being made by a real"
"8132" 45 "dressmaker over at Carmody. It’s to be done Saturday night, and I’m"
"8133" 45 "trying not to imagine myself walking up the church aisle on Sunday in"
"8134" 45 "my new suit and cap, because I’m afraid it isn’t right to imagine such"
"8135" 45 "things. But it just slips into my mind in spite of me. My cap is so"
"8136" 45 "pretty. Matthew bought it for me the day we were over at Carmody. It is"
"8137" 45 "one of those little blue velvet ones that are all the rage, with gold"
"8138" 45 "cord and tassels. Your new hat is elegant, Diana, and so becoming. When"
"8139" 45 "I saw you come into church last Sunday my heart swelled with pride to"
"8140" 45 "think you were my dearest friend. Do you suppose it’s wrong for us to"
"8141" 45 "think so much about our clothes? Marilla says it is very sinful. But it"
"8142" 45 "is such an interesting subject, isn’t it?”"
"8143" 45 ""
"8144" 45 "Marilla agreed to let Anne go to town, and it was arranged that"
"8145" 45 "Mr. Barry should take the girls in on the following Tuesday. As"
"8146" 45 "Charlottetown was thirty miles away and Mr. Barry wished to go and"

"8148" 45 "Anne counted it all joy, and was up before sunrise on Tuesday morning."
"8149" 45 "A glance from her window assured her that the day would be fine, for"
"8150" 45 "the eastern sky behind the firs of the Haunted Wood was all silvery"
"8151" 45 "and cloudless. Through the gap in the trees a light was shining in the"
"8152" 45 "western gable of Orchard Slope, a token that Diana was also up."
"8153" 45 ""
"8154" 45 "Anne was dressed by the time Matthew had the fire on and had the"
"8155" 45 "breakfast ready when Marilla came down, but for her own part was much"
"8156" 45 "too excited to eat. After breakfast the jaunty new cap and jacket were"

"8158" 45 "Orchard Slope. Mr. Barry and Diana were waiting for her, and they were"
"8159" 45 "soon on the road."
"8160" 45 ""
"8161" 45 "It was a long drive, but Anne and Diana enjoyed every minute of it. It"
"8162" 45 "was delightful to rattle along over the moist roads in the early red"
"8163" 45 "sunlight that was creeping across the shorn harvest fields. The air was"

"8171" 45 "seen; but wherever it went there was much of interest to discuss. It was"
"8172" 45 "almost noon when they reached town and found their way to “Beechwood.”"
"8173" 45 " It was quite a fine old mansion, set back from the street in a seclusion"
"8174" 45 "of green elms and branching beeches. Miss Barry met them at the door"
"8175" 45 "with a twinkle in her sharp black eyes."
"8176" 45 ""
"8177" 45 "“So you’ve come to see me at last, you Anne-girl,” she said. “Mercy,"

"8179" 45 "you’re ever so much better looking than you used to be, too. But I dare"
"8180" 45 "say you know that without being told.”"
"8181" 45 ""
"8182" 45 "“Indeed I didn’t,” said Anne radiantly. “I know I’m not so freckled as"
"8183" 45 "I used to be, so I’ve much to be thankful for, but I really hadn’t dared"
"8184" 45 "to hope there was any other improvement. I’m so glad you think there is,"
"8185" 45 "Miss Barry.” Miss Barry’s house was furnished with “great magnificence,”"
"8186" 45 " as Anne told Marilla afterward. The two little country girls were rather"
"8187" 45 "abashed by the splendor of the parlor where Miss Barry left them when"
"8188" 45 "she went to see about dinner."
"8189" 45 ""
"8190" 45 "“Isn’t it just like a palace?” whispered Diana. “I never was in Aunt"
"8191" 45 "Josephine’s house before, and I’d no idea it was so grand. I just wish"
"8192" 45 "Julia Bell could see this--she puts on such airs about her mother’s"
"8193" 45 "parlor.”"
"8194" 45 ""
"8195" 45 "“Velvet carpet,” sighed Anne luxuriously, “and silk curtains! I’ve"

"8201" 45 ""
"8202" 45 "Their sojourn in town was something that Anne and Diana dated from for"

"8204" 45 ""
"8205" 45 "On Wednesday Miss Barry took them to the Exhibition grounds and kept"
"8206" 45 "them there all day."
"8207" 45 ""

"8217" 45 "but I don’t see why. Do you? She said she would always think of it after"
"8218" 45 "this when he was praying so solemnly. Clara Louise MacPherson took a"

"8252" 45 ""

"8257" 45 ""

"8278" 45 "thing I’d rather be in the east gable at eleven, sound asleep, but kind"
"8279" 45 "of knowing even in my sleep that the stars were shining outside and that"

"8282" 45 "laughed at anything I said, even when I said the most solemn things. I"
"8283" 45 "don’t think I liked it, Marilla, because I wasn’t trying to be funny."
"8284" 45 "But she is a most hospitable lady and treated us royally.”"
"8285" 45 ""
"8286" 45 "Friday brought going-home time, and Mr. Barry drove in for the girls."
"8287" 45 ""
"8288" 45 "“Well, I hope you’ve enjoyed yourselves,” said Miss Barry, as she bade"
"8289" 45 "them good-bye."
"8290" 45 ""
"8291" 45 "“Indeed we have,” said Diana."
"8292" 45 ""
"8293" 45 "“And you, Anne-girl?”"
"8294" 45 ""
"8295" 45 "“I’ve enjoyed every minute of the time,” said Anne, throwing her arms"

"8297" 45 "Diana would never have dared to do such a thing and felt rather aghast"

"8299" 45 "veranda and watched the buggy out of sight. Then she went back into her"

"8307" 45 "winning ways, and the sweetness of her eyes and lips."
"8308" 45 ""
"8309" 45 "“I thought Marilla Cuthbert was an old fool when I heard she’d adopted"

"8313" 45 ""
"8314" 45 "Anne and Diana found the drive home as pleasant as the drive"

"8323" 45 ""

"8325" 45 ""

"8330" 45 "where a hot supper was waiting on the table."
"8331" 45 ""
"8332" 45 "“So you’ve got back?” said Marilla, folding up her knitting."
"8333" 45 ""

"8337" 45 ""

"8343" 45 ""

"8346" 45 ""

"8352" 45 "<CHAPTER XXX. The Queens Class Is Organized>"
"8353" 45 ""
"8354" 45 ""
"8355" 45 "MARILLA laid her knitting on her lap and leaned back in her chair. Her"
"8356" 45 "eyes were tired, and she thought vaguely that she must see about having"
"8357" 45 "her glasses changed the next time she went to town, for her eyes had"
"8358" 45 "grown tired very often of late."
"8359" 45 ""
"8360" 45 "It was nearly dark, for the full November twilight had fallen around"
"8361" 45 "Green Gables, and the only light in the kitchen came from the dancing"
"8362" 45 "red flames in the stove."
"8363" 45 ""
"8364" 45 "Anne was curled up Turk-fashion on the hearthrug, gazing into that"
"8365" 45 "joyous glow where the sunshine of a hundred summers was being distilled"
"8366" 45 "from the maple cordwood. She had been reading, but her book had slipped"
"8367" 45 "to the floor, and now she was dreaming, with a smile on her parted lips."
"8368" 45 "Glittering castles in Spain were shaping themselves out of the mists and"
"8369" 45 "rainbows of her lively fancy; adventures wonderful and enthralling"
"8370" 45 "were happening to her in cloudland--adventures that always turned out"
"8371" 45 "triumphantly and never involved her in scrapes like those of actual"
"8372" 45 "life."
"8373" 45 ""
"8374" 45 "Marilla looked at her with a tenderness that would never have been"
"8375" 45 "suffered to reveal itself in any clearer light than that soft mingling"
"8376" 45 "of fireshine and shadow. The lesson of a love that should display itself"
"8377" 45 "easily in spoken word and open look was one Marilla could never learn."
"8378" 45 "But she had learned to love this slim, gray-eyed girl with an affection"
"8379" 45 "all the deeper and stronger from its very undemonstrativeness. Her love"
"8380" 45 "made her afraid of being unduly indulgent, indeed. She had an uneasy"
"8381" 45 "feeling that it was rather sinful to set one’s heart so intensely on any"
"8382" 45 "human creature as she had set hers on Anne, and perhaps she performed a"
"8383" 45 "sort of unconscious penance for this by being stricter and more critical"
"8384" 45 "than if the girl had been less dear to her. Certainly Anne herself had"
"8385" 45 "no idea how Marilla loved her. She sometimes thought wistfully that"
"8386" 45 "Marilla was very hard to please and distinctly lacking in sympathy"
"8387" 45 "and understanding. But she always checked the thought reproachfully,"
"8388" 45 "remembering what she owed to Marilla."
"8389" 45 ""
"8390" 45 "“Anne,” said Marilla abruptly, “Miss Stacy was here this afternoon when"
"8391" 45 "you were out with Diana.”"
"8392" 45 ""
"8393" 45 "Anne came back from her other world with a start and a sigh."
"8394" 45 ""
"8395" 45 "“Was she? Oh, I’m so sorry I wasn’t in. Why didn’t you call me, Marilla?"
"8396" 45 "Diana and I were only over in the Haunted Wood. It’s lovely in the woods"
"8397" 45 "now. All the little wood things--the ferns and the satin leaves and the"

"8747" 45 "<CHAPTER XXXI. Where the Brook and River Meet>"
"8748" 45 ""
"8749" 45 ""
"8750" 45 "ANNE had her “good” summer and enjoyed it wholeheartedly. She and Diana"
"8751" 45 "fairly lived outdoors, reveling in all the delights that Lover’s Lane"
"8752" 45 "and the Dryad’s Bubble and Willowmere and Victoria Island afforded."
"8753" 45 "Marilla offered no objections to Anne’s gypsyings. The Spencervale"
"8754" 45 "doctor who had come the night Minnie May had the croup met Anne at the"
"8755" 45 "house of a patient one afternoon early in vacation, looked her over"
"8756" 45 "sharply, screwed up his mouth, shook his head, and sent a message to"
"8757" 45 "Marilla Cuthbert by another person. It was:"
"8758" 45 ""
"8759" 45 "“Keep that redheaded girl of yours in the open air all summer and don’t"
"8760" 45 "let her read books until she gets more spring into her step.”"
"8761" 45 ""
"8762" 45 "This message frightened Marilla wholesomely. She read Anne’s death"
"8763" 45 "warrant by consumption in it unless it was scrupulously obeyed. As a"
"8764" 45 "result, Anne had the golden summer of her life as far as freedom and"
"8765" 45 "frolic went. She walked, rowed, berried, and dreamed to her heart’s"
"8766" 45 "content; and when September came she was bright-eyed and alert, with a"
"8767" 45 "step that would have satisfied the Spencervale doctor and a heart full"
"8768" 45 "of ambition and zest once more."

"8770" 45 "“I feel just like studying with might and main,” she declared as she"

"9130" 45 "Moody Spurgeon still thinks he failed in history and Charlie says he"
"9131" 45 "failed in algebra. But we don’t really know anything about it and won’t"
"9132" 45 "until the pass list is out. That won’t be for a fortnight. Fancy living"
"9133" 45 "a fortnight in such suspense! I wish I could go to sleep and never wake"
"9134" 45 "up until it is over.”"
"9135" 45 ""
"9136" 45 "Diana knew it would be useless to ask how Gilbert Blythe had fared, so"
"9137" 45 "she merely said:"
"9138" 45 ""
"9139" 45 "“Oh, you’ll pass all right. Don’t worry.”"
"9140" 45 ""
"9141" 45 "“I’d rather not pass at all than not come out pretty well up on the"
"9142" 45 "list,” flashed Anne, by which she meant--and Diana knew she meant--that"
"9143" 45 "success would be incomplete and bitter if she did not come out ahead of"
"9144" 45 "Gilbert Blythe."
"9145" 45 ""
"9146" 45 "With this end in view Anne had strained every nerve during the"
"9147" 45 "examinations. So had Gilbert. They had met and passed each other on the"
"9148" 45 "street a dozen times without any sign of recognition and every time Anne"
"9149" 45 "had held her head a little higher and wished a little more earnestly"
"9150" 45 "that she had made friends with Gilbert when he asked her, and vowed a"
"9151" 45 "little more determinedly to surpass him in the examination. She knew"
"9152" 45 "that all Avonlea junior was wondering which would come out first; she"
"9153" 45 "even knew that Jimmy Glover and Ned Wright had a bet on the question"
"9154" 45 "and that Josie Pye had said there was no doubt in the world that Gilbert"
"9155" 45 "would be first; and she felt that her humiliation would be unbearable if"
"9156" 45 "she failed."
"9157" 45 ""
"9158" 45 "But she had another and nobler motive for wishing to do well. She wanted"
"9159" 45 "to “pass high” for the sake of Matthew and Marilla--especially Matthew."
"9160" 45 "Matthew had declared to her his conviction that she “would beat the"
"9161" 45 "whole Island.” That, Anne felt, was something it would be foolish to"
"9162" 45 "hope for even in the wildest dreams. But she did hope fervently that she"
"9163" 45 "would be among the first ten at least, so that she might see Matthew’s"
"9164" 45 "kindly brown eyes gleam with pride in her achievement. That, she"
"9165" 45 "felt, would be a sweet reward indeed for all her hard work and patient"
"9166" 45 "grubbing among unimaginative equations and conjugations."
"9167" 45 ""
"9168" 45 "At the end of the fortnight Anne took to “haunting” the post office"
"9169" 45 "also, in the distracted company of Jane, Ruby, and Josie, opening the"
"9170" 45 "Charlottetown dailies with shaking hands and cold, sinkaway feelings"
"9171" 45 "as bad as any experienced during the Entrance week. Charlie and Gilbert"
"9172" 45 "were not above doing this too, but Moody Spurgeon stayed resolutely"
"9173" 45 "away."
"9174" 45 ""
"9175" 45 "“I haven’t got the grit to go there and look at a paper in cold blood,”"
"9176" 45 " he told Anne. “I’m just going to wait until somebody comes and tells me"
"9177" 45 "suddenly whether I’ve passed or not.”"
"9178" 45 ""
"9179" 45 "When three weeks had gone by without the pass list appearing Anne began"
"9180" 45 "to feel that she really couldn’t stand the strain much longer. Her"
"9181" 45 "appetite failed and her interest in Avonlea doings languished."

"9187" 45 ""
"9188" 45 "But one evening the news came. Anne was sitting at her open window,"
"9189" 45 "for the time forgetful of the woes of examinations and the cares of the"

"9197" 45 ""

"9203" 45 ""

"9206" 45 ""

"9227" 45 ""

"9235" 45 ""

"9239" 45 ""

"9242" 45 ""

"9265" 45 "<CHAPTER XXXIII. The Hotel Concert>"
"9266" 45 ""
"9267" 45 ""
"9268" 45 "PUT on your white organdy, by all means, Anne,” advised Diana"
"9269" 45 "decidedly."
"9270" 45 ""
"9271" 45 "They were together in the east gable chamber; outside it was only"
"9272" 45 "twilight--a lovely yellowish-green twilight with a clear-blue cloudless"
"9273" 45 "sky. A big round moon, slowly deepening from her pallid luster into"
"9274" 45 "burnished silver, hung over the Haunted Wood; the air was full of sweet"
"9275" 45 "summer sounds--sleepy birds twittering, freakish breezes, faraway"
"9276" 45 "voices and laughter. But in Anne’s room the blind was drawn and the lamp"
"9277" 45 "lighted, for an important toilet was being made."
"9278" 45 ""
"9279" 45 "The east gable was a very different place from what it had been on that"
"9280" 45 "night four years before, when Anne had felt its bareness penetrate to"
"9281" 45 "the marrow of her spirit with its inhospitable chill. Changes had crept"
"9282" 45 "in, Marilla conniving at them resignedly, until it was as sweet and"
"9283" 45 "dainty a nest as a young girl could desire."
"9284" 45 ""
"9285" 45 "The velvet carpet with the pink roses and the pink silk curtains of"
"9286" 45 "Anne’s early visions had certainly never materialized; but her dreams"
"9287" 45 "had kept pace with her growth, and it is not probable she lamented"
"9288" 45 "them. The floor was covered with a pretty matting, and the curtains that"
"9289" 45 "softened the high window and fluttered in the vagrant breezes were of"
"9290" 45 "pale-green art muslin. The walls, hung not with gold and silver brocade"
"9291" 45 "tapestry, but with a dainty apple-blossom paper, were adorned with a few"
"9292" 45 "good pictures given Anne by Mrs. Allan. Miss Stacy’s photograph occupied"
"9293" 45 "the place of honor, and Anne made a sentimental point of keeping fresh"
"9294" 45 "flowers on the bracket under it. Tonight a spike of white lilies faintly"
"9295" 45 "perfumed the room like the dream of a fragrance. There was no “mahogany"
"9296" 45 "furniture,” but there was a white-painted bookcase filled with books, a"
"9297" 45 "cushioned wicker rocker, a toilet table befrilled with white muslin,"
"9298" 45 "a quaint, gilt-framed mirror with chubby pink Cupids and purple grapes"
"9299" 45 "painted over its arched top, that used to hang in the spare room, and a"
"9300" 45 "low white bed."
"9301" 45 ""
"9302" 45 "Anne was dressing for a concert at the White Sands Hotel. The guests had"
"9303" 45 "got it up in aid of the Charlottetown hospital, and had hunted out all"
"9304" 45 "the available amateur talent in the surrounding districts to help it"
"9305" 45 "along. Bertha Sampson and Pearl Clay of the White Sands Baptist choir"
"9306" 45 "had been asked to sing a duet; Milton Clark of Newbridge was to give a"
"9307" 45 "violin solo; Winnie Adella Blair of Carmody was to sing a Scotch ballad;"
"9308" 45 "and Laura Spencer of Spencervale and Anne Shirley of Avonlea were to"
"9309" 45 "recite."
"9310" 45 ""
"9311" 45 "As Anne would have said at one time, it was “an epoch in her life,” and"
"9312" 45 "she was deliciously athrill with the excitement of it. Matthew was in"
"9313" 45 "the seventh heaven of gratified pride over the honor conferred on his"
"9314" 45 "Anne and Marilla was not far behind, although she would have died rather"
"9315" 45 "than admit it, and said she didn’t think it was very proper for a lot"
"9316" 45 "of young folks to be gadding over to the hotel without any responsible"
"9317" 45 "person with them."
"9318" 45 ""
"9319" 45 "Anne and Diana were to drive over with Jane Andrews and her brother"
"9320" 45 "Billy in their double-seated buggy; and several other Avonlea girls and"
"9321" 45 "boys were going too. There was a party of visitors expected out from"
"9322" 45 "town, and after the concert a supper was to be given to the performers."
"9323" 45 ""
"9324" 45 "“Do you really think the organdy will be best?” queried Anne anxiously."
"9325" 45 "“I don’t think it’s as pretty as my blue-flowered muslin--and it"
"9326" 45 "certainly isn’t so fashionable.”"
"9327" 45 ""

"9330" 45 "dressed up. But the organdy seems as if it grew on you.”"
"9331" 45 ""

"9334" 45 "sought after. She was looking very pretty herself on this particular"

"9337" 45 "her appearance was of minor importance. All her pains were bestowed upon"
"9338" 45 "Anne, who, she vowed, must, for the credit of Avonlea, be dressed and"
"9339" 45 "combed and adorned to the Queen’s taste."
"9340" 45 ""
"9341" 45 "“Pull out that frill a little more--so; here, let me tie your sash; now"

"9352" 45 ""

"9356" 45 ""

"9450" 45 ""
"9451" 45 "It was still worse on the platform of the big concert hall of the hotel,"

"9453" 45 "the perfume and hum bewildered her. She wished she were sitting down"
"9454" 45 "in the audience with Diana and Jane, who seemed to be having a splendid"

"9457" 45 "lady occasionally turned her head squarely around and surveyed Anne"
"9458" 45 "through her eyeglasses until Anne, acutely sensitive of being so"

"9460" 45 "kept talking audibly to her next neighbor about the “country bumpkins”"
"9461" 45 " and “rustic belles” in the audience, languidly anticipating “such fun”"
"9462" 45 " from the displays of local talent on the program. Anne believed that she"
"9463" 45 "would hate that white-lace girl to the end of life."
"9464" 45 ""
"9465" 45 "Unfortunately for Anne, a professional elocutionist was staying at the"
"9466" 45 "hotel and had consented to recite. She was a lithe, dark-eyed woman in a"
"9467" 45 "wonderful gown of shimmering gray stuff like woven moonbeams, with gems"
"9468" 45 "on her neck and in her dark hair. She had a marvelously flexible voice"

"9473" 45 "recite after that--never. Had she ever thought she could recite? Oh, if"
"9474" 45 "she were only back at Green Gables!"
"9475" 45 ""
"9476" 45 "At this unpropitious moment her name was called. Somehow Anne--who did"
"9477" 45 "not notice the rather guilty little start of surprise the white-lace"

"9480" 45 "She was so pale that Diana and Jane, down in the audience, clasped each"

"9482" 45 ""
"9483" 45 "Anne was the victim of an overwhelming attack of stage fright. Often as"

"9495" 45 "have fled from the platform despite the humiliation which, she felt,"
"9496" 45 "must ever after be her portion if she did so."
"9497" 45 ""
"9498" 45 "But suddenly, as her dilated, frightened eyes gazed out over the"

"9503" 45 "of the effect produced by Anne’s slender white form and spiritual face"
"9504" 45 "against a background of palms in particular. Josie Pye, whom he had"
"9505" 45 "driven over, sat beside him, and her face certainly was both triumphant"
"9506" 45 "and taunting. But Anne did not see Josie, and would not have cared if"
"9507" 45 "she had. She drew a long breath and flung her head up proudly, courage"
"9508" 45 "and determination tingling over her like an electric shock. She _would"
"9509" 45 "not_ fail before Gilbert Blythe--he should never be able to laugh at her,"
"9510" 45 "never, never! Her fright and nervousness vanished; and she began her"
"9511" 45 "recitation, her clear, sweet voice reaching to the farthest corner of"
"9512" 45 "the room without a tremor or a break. Self-possession was fully restored"
"9513" 45 "to her, and in the reaction from that horrible moment of powerlessness"
"9514" 45 "she recited as she had never done before. When she finished there were"
"9515" 45 "bursts of honest applause. Anne, stepping back to her seat, blushing"
"9516" 45 "with shyness and delight, found her hand vigorously clasped and shaken"
"9517" 45 "by the stout lady in pink silk."
"9518" 45 ""
"9519" 45 "“My dear, you did splendidly,” she puffed. “I’ve been crying like a"
"9520" 45 "baby, actually I have. There, they’re encoring you--they’re bound to"
"9521" 45 "have you back!”"
"9522" 45 ""
"9523" 45 "“Oh, I can’t go,” said Anne confusedly. “But yet--I must, or Matthew"
"9524" 45 "will be disappointed. He said they would encore me.”"
"9525" 45 ""
"9526" 45 "“Then don’t disappoint Matthew,” said the pink lady, laughing."
"9527" 45 ""
"9528" 45 "Smiling, blushing, limpid eyed, Anne tripped back and gave a quaint,"
"9529" 45 "funny little selection that captivated her audience still further. The"
"9530" 45 "rest of the evening was quite a little triumph for her."
"9531" 45 ""
"9532" 45 "When the concert was over, the stout, pink lady--who was the wife of"
"9533" 45 "an American millionaire--took her under her wing, and introduced her"
"9534" 45 "to everybody; and everybody was very nice to her. The professional"
"9535" 45 "elocutionist, Mrs. Evans, came and chatted with her, telling her that"
"9536" 45 "she had a charming voice and “interpreted” her selections beautifully."
"9537" 45 "Even the white-lace girl paid her a languid little compliment. They had"
"9538" 45 "supper in the big, beautifully decorated dining room; Diana and Jane"
"9539" 45 "were invited to partake of this, also, since they had come with Anne,"
"9540" 45 "but Billy was nowhere to be found, having decamped in mortal fear"
"9541" 45 "of some such invitation. He was in waiting for them, with the team,"
"9542" 45 "however, when it was all over, and the three girls came merrily out into"
"9543" 45 "the calm, white moonshine radiance. Anne breathed deeply, and looked"
"9544" 45 "into the clear sky beyond the dark boughs of the firs."
"9545" 45 ""
"9546" 45 "Oh, it was good to be out again in the purity and silence of the night!"
"9547" 45 "How great and still and wonderful everything was, with the murmur of the"
"9548" 45 "sea sounding through it and the darkling cliffs beyond like grim giants"
"9549" 45 "guarding enchanted coasts."
"9550" 45 ""
"9551" 45 "“Hasn’t it been a perfectly splendid time?” sighed Jane, as they drove"
"9552" 45 "away. “I just wish I was a rich American and could spend my summer at"
"9553" 45 "a hotel and wear jewels and low-necked dresses and have ice cream and"
"9554" 45 "chicken salad every blessed day. I’m sure it would be ever so much"
"9555" 45 "more fun than teaching school. Anne, your recitation was simply great,"
"9556" 45 "although I thought at first you were never going to begin. I think it"
"9557" 45 "was better than Mrs. Evans’s.”"
"9558" 45 ""
"9559" 45 "“Oh, no, don’t say things like that, Jane,” said Anne quickly, “because"
"9560" 45 "it sounds silly. It couldn’t be better than Mrs. Evans’s, you know, for"
"9561" 45 "she is a professional, and I’m only a schoolgirl, with a little knack"
"9562" 45 "of reciting. I’m quite satisfied if the people just liked mine pretty"
"9563" 45 "well.”"
"9564" 45 ""
"9565" 45 "“I’ve a compliment for you, Anne,” said Diana. “At least I think it"
"9566" 45 "must be a compliment because of the tone he said it in. Part of it"
"9567" 45 "was anyhow. There was an American sitting behind Jane and me--such a"
"9568" 45 "romantic-looking man, with coal-black hair and eyes. Josie Pye says he"
"9569" 45 "is a distinguished artist, and that her mother’s cousin in Boston is"
"9570" 45 "married to a man that used to go to school with him. Well, we heard"
"9571" 45 "him say--didn’t we, Jane?--‘Who is that girl on the platform with the"

"9573" 45 "Anne. But what does Titian hair mean?”"
"9574" 45 ""
"9575" 45 "“Being interpreted it means plain red, I guess,” laughed Anne. “Titian"
"9576" 45 "was a very famous artist who liked to paint red-haired women.”"
"9577" 45 ""
"9578" 45 "“_Did_ you see all the diamonds those ladies wore?” sighed Jane. “They"
"9579" 45 "were simply dazzling. Wouldn’t you just love to be rich, girls?”"
"9580" 45 ""
"9581" 45 "“We _are_ rich,” said Anne staunchly. “Why, we have sixteen years to our"

"9584" 45 "things not seen. We couldn’t enjoy its loveliness any more if we had"

"9586" 45 "of those women if you could. Would you want to be that white-lace girl"
"9587" 45 "and wear a sour look all your life, as if you’d been born turning up"
"9588" 45 "your nose at the world? Or the pink lady, kind and nice as she is, so"
"9589" 45 "stout and short that you’d really no figure at all? Or even Mrs. Evans,"
"9590" 45 "with that sad, sad look in her eyes? She must have been dreadfully"
"9591" 45 "unhappy sometime to have such a look. You _know_ you wouldn’t, Jane"
"9592" 45 "Andrews!”"
"9593" 45 ""
"9594" 45 "“I _don’t_ know--exactly,” said Jane unconvinced. “I think diamonds would"
"9595" 45 "comfort a person for a good deal.”"
"9596" 45 ""
"9597" 45 "“Well, I don’t want to be anyone but myself, even if I go uncomforted by"
"9598" 45 "diamonds all my life,” declared Anne. “I’m quite content to be Anne of"
"9599" 45 "Green Gables, with my string of pearl beads. I know Matthew gave me as"
"9600" 45 "much love with them as ever went with Madame the Pink Lady’s jewels.”"
"9601" 45 ""

"9605" 45 "<CHAPTER XXXIV. A Queen’s Girl>"
"9606" 45 ""
"9607" 45 ""
"9608" 45 "THE next three weeks were busy ones at Green Gables, for Anne was"
"9609" 45 "getting ready to go to Queen’s, and there was much sewing to be done,"
"9610" 45 "and many things to be talked over and arranged. Anne’s outfit was"
"9611" 45 "ample and pretty, for Matthew saw to that, and Marilla for once made"
"9612" 45 "no objections whatever to anything he purchased or suggested. More--one"
"9613" 45 "evening she went up to the east gable with her arms full of a delicate"
"9614" 45 "pale green material."
"9615" 45 ""
"9616" 45 "“Anne, here’s something for a nice light dress for you. I don’t suppose"
"9617" 45 "you really need it; you’ve plenty of pretty waists; but I thought maybe"
"9618" 45 "you’d like something real dressy to wear if you were asked out anywhere"
"9619" 45 "of an evening in town, to a party or anything like that. I hear that"
"9620" 45 "Jane and Ruby and Josie have got ‘evening dresses,’ as they call them,"
"9621" 45 "and I don’t mean you shall be behind them. I got Mrs. Allan to help me"
"9622" 45 "pick it in town last week, and we’ll get Emily Gillis to make it for"
"9623" 45 "you. Emily has got taste, and her fits aren’t to be equaled.”"
"9624" 45 ""
"9625" 45 "“Oh, Marilla, it’s just lovely,” said Anne. “Thank you so much. I don’t"
"9626" 45 "believe you ought to be so kind to me--it’s making it harder every day"
"9627" 45 "for me to go away.”"
"9628" 45 ""
"9629" 45 "The green dress was made up with as many tucks and frills and shirrings"
"9630" 45 "as Emily’s taste permitted. Anne put it on one evening for Matthew’s"
"9631" 45 "and Marilla’s benefit, and recited “The Maiden’s Vow” for them in the"
"9632" 45 "kitchen. As Marilla watched the bright, animated face and graceful"
"9633" 45 "motions her thoughts went back to the evening Anne had arrived at Green"
"9634" 45 "Gables, and memory recalled a vivid picture of the odd, frightened child"
"9635" 45 "in her preposterous yellowish-brown wincey dress, the heartbreak looking"
"9636" 45 "out of her tearful eyes. Something in the memory brought tears to"
"9637" 45 "Marilla’s own eyes."
"9638" 45 ""
"9639" 45 "“I declare, my recitation has made you cry, Marilla,” said Anne gaily"
"9640" 45 "stooping over Marilla’s chair to drop a butterfly kiss on that lady’s"
"9641" 45 "cheek. “Now, I call that a positive triumph.”"
"9642" 45 ""
"9643" 45 "“No, I wasn’t crying over your piece,” said Marilla, who would have"
"9644" 45 "scorned to be betrayed into such weakness by any poetry stuff. “I just"
"9645" 45 "couldn’t help thinking of the little girl you used to be, Anne. And"
"9646" 45 "I was wishing you could have stayed a little girl, even with all your"
"9647" 45 "queer ways. You’ve grown up now and you’re going away; and you look so"
"9648" 45 "tall and stylish and so--so--different altogether in that dress--as if"
"9649" 45 "you didn’t belong in Avonlea at all--and I just got lonesome thinking it"
"9650" 45 "all over.”"
"9651" 45 ""
"9652" 45 "“Marilla!” Anne sat down on Marilla’s gingham lap, took Marilla’s lined"
"9653" 45 "face between her hands, and looked gravely and tenderly into Marilla’s"
"9654" 45 "eyes. “I’m not a bit changed--not really. I’m only just pruned down and"
"9655" 45 "branched out. The real _me_--back here--is just the same. It won’t make a"
"9656" 45 "bit of difference where I go or how much I change outwardly; at heart I"
"9657" 45 "shall always be your little Anne, who will love you and Matthew and dear"
"9658" 45 "Green Gables more and better every day of her life.”"
"9659" 45 ""
"9660" 45 "Anne laid her fresh young cheek against Marilla’s faded one, and reached"
"9661" 45 "out a hand to pat Matthew’s shoulder. Marilla would have given much just"
"9662" 45 "then to have possessed Anne’s power of putting her feelings into words;"
"9663" 45 "but nature and habit had willed it otherwise, and she could only put her"
"9664" 45 "arms close about her girl and hold her tenderly to her heart, wishing"
"9665" 45 "that she need never let her go."
"9666" 45 ""
"9667" 45 "Matthew, with a suspicious moisture in his eyes, got up and went"
"9668" 45 "out-of-doors. Under the stars of the blue summer night he walked"
"9669" 45 "agitatedly across the yard to the gate under the poplars."
"9670" 45 ""
"9671" 45 "“Well now, I guess she ain’t been much spoiled,” he muttered, proudly."
"9672" 45 "“I guess my putting in my oar occasional never did much harm after all."
"9673" 45 "She’s smart and pretty, and loving, too, which is better than all the"
"9674" 45 "rest. She’s been a blessing to us, and there never was a luckier mistake"
"9675" 45 "than what Mrs. Spencer made--if it _was_ luck. I don’t believe it was any"
"9676" 45 "such thing. It was Providence, because the Almighty saw we needed her, I"
"9677" 45 "reckon.”"
"9678" 45 ""
"9679" 45 "The day finally came when Anne must go to town. She and Matthew drove"
"9680" 45 "in one fine September morning, after a tearful parting with Diana and an"
"9681" 45 "untearful practical one--on Marilla’s side at least--with Marilla. But"
"9682" 45 "when Anne had gone Diana dried her tears and went to a beach picnic at"
"9683" 45 "White Sands with some of her Carmody cousins, where she contrived"
"9684" 45 "to enjoy herself tolerably well; while Marilla plunged fiercely into"
"9685" 45 "unnecessary work and kept at it all day long with the bitterest kind of"
"9686" 45 "heartache--the ache that burns and gnaws and cannot wash itself away"
"9687" 45 "in ready tears. But that night, when Marilla went to bed, acutely and"
"9688" 45 "miserably conscious that the little gable room at the end of the"
"9689" 45 "hall was untenanted by any vivid young life and unstirred by any soft"
"9690" 45 "breathing, she buried her face in her pillow, and wept for her girl in"
"9691" 45 "a passion of sobs that appalled her when she grew calm enough to reflect"
"9692" 45 "how very wicked it must be to take on so about a sinful fellow creature."
"9693" 45 ""
"9694" 45 "Anne and the rest of the Avonlea scholars reached town just in time to"
"9695" 45 "hurry off to the Academy. That first day passed pleasantly enough in a"
"9696" 45 "whirl of excitement, meeting all the new students, learning to know the"
"9697" 45 "professors by sight and being assorted and organized into classes. Anne"
"9698" 45 "intended taking up the Second Year work being advised to do so by Miss"
"9699" 45 "Stacy; Gilbert Blythe elected to do the same. This meant getting a"
"9700" 45 "First Class teacher’s license in one year instead of two, if they were"
"9701" 45 "successful; but it also meant much more and harder work. Jane, Ruby,"
"9702" 45 "Josie, Charlie, and Moody Spurgeon, not being troubled with the"
"9703" 45 "stirrings of ambition, were content to take up the Second Class work."
"9704" 45 "Anne was conscious of a pang of loneliness when she found herself in"
"9705" 45 "a room with fifty other students, not one of whom she knew, except the"
"9706" 45 "tall, brown-haired boy across the room; and knowing him in the fashion"
"9707" 45 "she did, did not help her much, as she reflected pessimistically."
"9708" 45 "Yet she was undeniably glad that they were in the same class; the old"
"9709" 45 "rivalry could still be carried on, and Anne would hardly have known what"
"9710" 45 "to do if it had been lacking."
"9711" 45 ""
"9712" 45 "“I wouldn’t feel comfortable without it,” she thought. “Gilbert looks"
"9713" 45 "awfully determined. I suppose he’s making up his mind, here and now, to"
"9714" 45 "win the medal. What a splendid chin he has! I never noticed it before."
"9715" 45 "I do wish Jane and Ruby had gone in for First Class, too. I suppose I"
"9716" 45 "won’t feel so much like a cat in a strange garret when I get acquainted,"
"9717" 45 "though. I wonder which of the girls here are going to be my friends."
"9718" 45 "It’s really an interesting speculation. Of course I promised Diana that"
"9719" 45 "no Queen’s girl, no matter how much I liked her, should ever be as dear"
"9720" 45 "to me as she is; but I’ve lots of second-best affections to bestow. I"
"9721" 45 "like the look of that girl with the brown eyes and the crimson waist."
"9722" 45 "She looks vivid and red-rosy; there’s that pale, fair one gazing out of"
"9723" 45 "the window. She has lovely hair, and looks as if she knew a thing or two"
"9724" 45 "about dreams. I’d like to know them both--know them well--well enough to"
"9725" 45 "walk with my arm about their waists, and call them nicknames. But just"
"9726" 45 "now I don’t know them and they don’t know me, and probably don’t want to"
"9727" 45 "know me particularly. Oh, it’s lonesome!”"
"9728" 45 ""
"9729" 45 "It was lonesomer still when Anne found herself alone in her hall bedroom"
"9730" 45 "that night at twilight. She was not to board with the other girls, who"
"9731" 45 "all had relatives in town to take pity on them. Miss Josephine Barry"
"9732" 45 "would have liked to board her, but Beechwood was so far from the"
"9733" 45 "Academy that it was out of the question; so Miss Barry hunted up a"
"9734" 45 "boarding-house, assuring Matthew and Marilla that it was the very place"
"9735" 45 "for Anne."
"9736" 45 ""
"9737" 45 "“The lady who keeps it is a reduced gentlewoman,” explained Miss Barry."
"9738" 45 "“Her husband was a British officer, and she is very careful what sort"
"9739" 45 "of boarders she takes. Anne will not meet with any objectionable persons"
"9740" 45 "under her roof. The table is good, and the house is near the Academy, in"
"9741" 45 "a quiet neighborhood.”"
"9742" 45 ""
"9743" 45 "All this might be quite true, and indeed, proved to be so, but it did"
"9744" 45 "not materially help Anne in the first agony of homesickness that seized"
"9745" 45 "upon her. She looked dismally about her narrow little room, with its"
"9746" 45 "dull-papered, pictureless walls, its small iron bedstead and empty"
"9747" 45 "book-case; and a horrible choke came into her throat as she thought of"
"9748" 45 "her own white room at Green Gables, where she would have the pleasant"
"9749" 45 "consciousness of a great green still outdoors, of sweet peas growing in"
"9750" 45 "the garden, and moonlight falling on the orchard, of the brook below the"
"9751" 45 "slope and the spruce boughs tossing in the night wind beyond it, of a"
"9752" 45 "vast starry sky, and the light from Diana’s window shining out through"
"9753" 45 "the gap in the trees. Here there was nothing of this; Anne knew that"
"9754" 45 "outside of her window was a hard street, with a network of telephone"
"9755" 45 "wires shutting out the sky, the tramp of alien feet, and a thousand"
"9756" 45 "lights gleaming on stranger faces. She knew that she was going to cry,"
"9757" 45 "and fought against it."
"9758" 45 ""
"9759" 45 "“I _won’t_ cry. It’s silly--and weak--there’s the third tear splashing"
"9760" 45 "down by my nose. There are more coming! I must think of something funny"
"9761" 45 "to stop them. But there’s nothing funny except what is connected with"
"9762" 45 "Avonlea, and that only makes things worse--four--five--I’m going home"
"9763" 45 "next Friday, but that seems a hundred years away. Oh, Matthew is nearly"
"9764" 45 "home by now--and Marilla is at the gate, looking down the lane for"
"9765" 45 "him--six--seven--eight--oh, there’s no use in counting them! They’re"
"9766" 45 "coming in a flood presently. I can’t cheer up--I don’t _want_ to cheer up."
"9767" 45 "It’s nicer to be miserable!”"
"9768" 45 ""
"9769" 45 "The flood of tears would have come, no doubt, had not Josie Pye appeared"
"9770" 45 "at that moment. In the joy of seeing a familiar face Anne forgot that"
"9771" 45 "there had never been much love lost between her and Josie. As a part of"
"9772" 45 "Avonlea life even a Pye was welcome."
"9773" 45 ""
"9774" 45 "“I’m so glad you came up,” Anne said sincerely."
"9775" 45 ""
"9776" 45 "“You’ve been crying,” remarked Josie, with aggravating pity. “I suppose"
"9777" 45 "you’re homesick--some people have so little self-control in that"
"9778" 45 "respect. I’ve no intention of being homesick, I can tell you. Town’s too"
"9779" 45 "jolly after that poky old Avonlea. I wonder how I ever existed there so"
"9780" 45 "long. You shouldn’t cry, Anne; it isn’t becoming, for your nose and eyes"
"9781" 45 "get red, and then you seem _all_ red. I’d a perfectly scrumptious time in"
"9782" 45 "the Academy today. Our French professor is simply a duck. His moustache"
"9783" 45 "would give you kerwollowps of the heart. Have you anything eatable"

"9786" 45 "gone to the park to hear the band play with Frank Stockley. He boards"
"9787" 45 "same place as I do, and he’s a sport. He noticed you in class today, and"
"9788" 45 "asked me who the red-headed girl was. I told him you were an orphan that"
"9789" 45 "the Cuthberts had adopted, and nobody knew very much about what you’d"
"9790" 45 "been before that.”"
"9791" 45 ""
"9792" 45 "Anne was wondering if, after all, solitude and tears were not more"
"9793" 45 "satisfactory than Josie Pye’s companionship when Jane and Ruby appeared,"
"9794" 45 "each with an inch of Queen’s color ribbon--purple and scarlet--pinned"

"9796" 45 "had to subside into comparative harmlessness."
"9797" 45 ""

"9806" 45 "Avonlea flavor.”"
"9807" 45 ""
"9808" 45 "Ruby, perceiving the Queen’s calendar lying on the table, wanted to know"
"9809" 45 "if Anne meant to try for the gold medal."
"9810" 45 ""
"9811" 45 "Anne blushed and admitted she was thinking of it."
"9812" 45 ""
"9813" 45 "“Oh, that reminds me,” said Josie, “Queen’s is to get one of the Avery"
"9814" 45 "scholarships after all. The word came today. Frank Stockley told me--his"
"9815" 45 "uncle is one of the board of governors, you know. It will be announced"

"9817" 45 ""
"9818" 45 "An Avery scholarship! Anne felt her heart beat more quickly, and the"
"9819" 45 "horizons of her ambition shifted and broadened as if by magic. Before"

"9826" 45 "that here her foot was on native heath."
"9827" 45 ""
"9828" 45 "A wealthy manufacturer of New Brunswick had died and left part of his"
"9829" 45 "fortune to endow a large number of scholarships to be distributed"
"9830" 45 "among the various high schools and academies of the Maritime Provinces,"
"9831" 45 "according to their respective standings. There had been much doubt"
"9832" 45 "whether one would be allotted to Queen’s, but the matter was settled at"
"9833" 45 "last, and at the end of the year the graduate who made the highest mark"
"9834" 45 "in English and English Literature would win the scholarship--two hundred"
"9835" 45 "and fifty dollars a year for four years at Redmond College. No wonder"
"9836" 45 "that Anne went to bed that night with tingling cheeks!"
"9837" 45 ""
"9838" 45 "“I’ll win that scholarship if hard work can do it,” she resolved."
"9839" 45 "“Wouldn’t Matthew be proud if I got to be a B.A.? Oh, it’s delightful to"
"9840" 45 "have ambitions. I’m so glad I have such a lot. And there never seems to"
"9841" 45 "be any end to them--that’s the best of it. Just as soon as you attain"
"9842" 45 "to one ambition you see another one glittering higher up still. It does"
"9843" 45 "make life so interesting.”"
"9844" 45 ""
"9845" 45 ""

"9848" 45 "<CHAPTER XXXV. The Winter at Queen’s>"
"9849" 45 ""
"9850" 45 ""
"9851" 45 "ANNE’S homesickness wore off, greatly helped in the wearing by her"
"9852" 45 "weekend visits home. As long as the open weather lasted the Avonlea"
"9853" 45 "students went out to Carmody on the new branch railway every Friday"
"9854" 45 "night. Diana and several other Avonlea young folks were generally on"
"9855" 45 "hand to meet them and they all walked over to Avonlea in a merry party."
"9856" 45 "Anne thought those Friday evening gypsyings over the autumnal hills in"
"9857" 45 "the crisp golden air, with the homelights of Avonlea twinkling beyond,"
"9858" 45 "were the best and dearest hours in the whole week."
"9859" 45 ""
"9860" 45 "Gilbert Blythe nearly always walked with Ruby Gillis and carried her"
"9861" 45 "satchel for her. Ruby was a very handsome young lady, now thinking"
"9862" 45 "herself quite as grown up as she really was; she wore her skirts as long"
"9863" 45 "as her mother would let her and did her hair up in town, though she had"
"9864" 45 "to take it down when she went home. She had large, bright-blue eyes,"
"9865" 45 "a brilliant complexion, and a plump showy figure. She laughed a great"
"9866" 45 "deal, was cheerful and good-tempered, and enjoyed the pleasant things of"
"9867" 45 "life frankly."
"9868" 45 ""
"9869" 45 "“But I shouldn’t think she was the sort of girl Gilbert would like,”"
"9870" 45 " whispered Jane to Anne. Anne did not think so either, but she would not"
"9871" 45 "have said so for the Avery scholarship. She could not help thinking,"
"9872" 45 "too, that it would be very pleasant to have such a friend as Gilbert"
"9873" 45 "to jest and chatter with and exchange ideas about books and studies and"
"9874" 45 "ambitions. Gilbert had ambitions, she knew, and Ruby Gillis did not seem"
"9875" 45 "the sort of person with whom such could be profitably discussed."
"9876" 45 ""
"9877" 45 "There was no silly sentiment in Anne’s ideas concerning Gilbert. Boys"
"9878" 45 "were to her, when she thought about them at all, merely possible good"
"9879" 45 "comrades. If she and Gilbert had been friends she would not have cared"
"9880" 45 "how many other friends he had nor with whom he walked. She had a genius"
"9881" 45 "for friendship; girl friends she had in plenty; but she had a vague"
"9882" 45 "consciousness that masculine friendship might also be a good thing"
"9883" 45 "to round out one’s conceptions of companionship and furnish broader"

"9886" 45 "that if Gilbert had ever walked home with her from the train, over the"

"9889" 45 "around them and their hopes and ambitions therein. Gilbert was a clever"
"9890" 45 "young fellow, with his own thoughts about things and a determination to"
"9891" 45 "get the best out of life and put the best into it. Ruby Gillis told Jane"
"9892" 45 "Andrews that she didn’t understand half the things Gilbert Blythe said;"
"9893" 45 "he talked just like Anne Shirley did when she had a thoughtful fit on"
"9894" 45 "and for her part she didn’t think it any fun to be bothering about books"
"9895" 45 "and that sort of thing when you didn’t have to. Frank Stockley had lots"
"9896" 45 "more dash and go, but then he wasn’t half as good-looking as Gilbert and"
"9897" 45 "she really couldn’t decide which she liked best!"
"9898" 45 ""
"9899" 45 "In the Academy Anne gradually drew a little circle of friends about"
"9900" 45 "her, thoughtful, imaginative, ambitious students like herself. With the"
"9901" 45 "“rose-red” girl, Stella Maynard, and the “dream girl,” Priscilla Grant,"

"9905" 45 "as aerial and rainbow-like as Anne’s own."
"9906" 45 ""
"9907" 45 "After the Christmas holidays the Avonlea students gave up going home"
"9908" 45 "on Fridays and settled down to hard work. By this time all the Queen’s"

"9915" 45 "winner. The bronze medal for mathematics was considered as good as"
"9916" 45 "won by a fat, funny little up-country boy with a bumpy forehead and a"

"9918" 45 ""
"9919" 45 "Ruby Gillis was the handsomest girl of the year at the Academy; in the"

"9927" 45 "pupils held their own in the wider arena of the academical course."
"9928" 45 ""
"9929" 45 "Anne worked hard and steadily. Her rivalry with Gilbert was as intense"

"9936" 45 ""
"9937" 45 "In spite of lessons the students found opportunities for pleasant times."
"9938" 45 "Anne spent many of her spare hours at Beechwood and generally ate her"
"9939" 45 "Sunday dinners there and went to church with Miss Barry. The latter was,"

"9943" 45 "old lady."
"9944" 45 ""

"9951" 45 ""
"9952" 45 "Then, almost before anybody realized it, spring had come; out in"

"9957" 45 ""

"9965" 45 ""

"9973" 45 ""

"9998" 45 ""

"10011" 45 "<CHAPTER XXXVI. The Glory and the Dream>"
"10012" 45 ""
"10013" 45 ""
"10014" 45 "ON the morning when the final results of all the examinations were to be"
"10015" 45 "posted on the bulletin board at Queen’s, Anne and Jane walked down the"
"10016" 45 "street together. Jane was smiling and happy; examinations were over"
"10017" 45 "and she was comfortably sure she had made a pass at least; further"
"10018" 45 "considerations troubled Jane not at all; she had no soaring ambitions"
"10019" 45 "and consequently was not affected with the unrest attendant thereon. For"
"10020" 45 "we pay a price for everything we get or take in this world; and although"
"10021" 45 "ambitions are well worth having, they are not to be cheaply won, but"
"10022" 45 "exact their dues of work and self-denial, anxiety and discouragement."
"10023" 45 "Anne was pale and quiet; in ten more minutes she would know who had"
"10024" 45 "won the medal and who the Avery. Beyond those ten minutes there did not"
"10025" 45 "seem, just then, to be anything worth being called Time."
"10026" 45 ""
"10027" 45 "“Of course you’ll win one of them anyhow,” said Jane, who couldn’t"
"10028" 45 "understand how the faculty could be so unfair as to order it otherwise."
"10029" 45 ""

"10031" 45 "will win it. And I’m not going to march up to that bulletin board and"

"10037" 45 "sympathize with me. Promise me this, Jane.”"
"10038" 45 ""

"10228" 45 "<CHAPTER XXXVII. The Reaper Whose Name Is Death>"
"10229" 45 ""
"10230" 45 ""
"10231" 45 "MATTHEW--Matthew--what is the matter? Matthew, are you sick?”"
"10232" 45 ""

"10241" 45 ""

"10474" 45 "MARILLA went to town the next day and returned in the evening. Anne had"
"10475" 45 "gone over to Orchard Slope with Diana and came back to find Marilla in"
"10476" 45 "the kitchen, sitting by the table with her head leaning on her hand."

"10478" 45 "had never seen Marilla sit limply inert like that."
"10479" 45 ""

"10481" 45 ""

"10483" 45 "am tired but I haven’t thought about it. It’s not that.”"
"10484" 45 ""

"10486" 45 ""
"10487" 45 "“Yes, I saw him. He examined my eyes. He says that if I give up all"
"10488" 45 "reading and sewing entirely and any kind of work that strains the eyes,"
"10489" 45 "and if I’m careful not to cry, and if I wear the glasses he’s given me"
"10490" 45 "he thinks my eyes may not get any worse and my headaches will be cured."
"10491" 45 "But if I don’t he says I’ll certainly be stone-blind in six months."
"10492" 45 "Blind! Anne, just think of it!”"
"10493" 45 ""
